Norm,

    I'm no longer running Red Hat here so I don't have 'man rpm'. But, the
syntax is something like
  	rpm -q --what provides <file_name>

Or, you could wander over to rpmfind.net and ask for the file there. It will
return the list of available packages that contain it.

From carla at bratgrrl.com  Tue Feb  1 11:48:27 2005
From: carla at bratgrrl.com (Carla Schroder)
Date: Tue, 1 Feb 2005 11:48:27 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] CD-R, label?
In-Reply-To: <1107286391.29180.1.camel@apollo.spears.org>
References: <1107286391.29180.1.camel@apollo.spears.org>
Message-ID: <200502011148.28738.carla@bratgrrl.com>

On Tuesday 01 February 2005 11:33 am, Bill Spears wrote:
> I use mkisofs and cdrecord to write CD-R's. ?How do I give a label to
> the CDROM.
> 
> My OS is Fedora 3.

Use the -V option for mkisofs, like 

mkisofs <other options> -V data_disk

'data_disk' will show up in winderz explorer as the disk name.

There are a couple other options you might be interested in.

-publisher <foo> lets you insert a text string into the volume header, like 
"Bill's Productions, you copy you die." You can specify a default -publisher 
tag in .mkisofsrc, with PUBL=<foo>

-p <foo> is the preparer ID. Something like "this awesome disk prepared by 
Bill's lackey on 2-1-2005." This also can have a default in .mkisofsrc, 
PREP=<foo>. Command-line overrides the defaults.

man mkisofs tells all.

In-Reply-To: <1107286391.29180.1.camel@apollo.spears.org>

On Tue, 1 Feb 2005, Bill Spears wrote:

> I use mkisofs and cdrecord to write CD-R's.  How do I give a label to
> the CDROM.

   Bow down, approach slowly with the label held visibly in front of you and
feed gently. Well-trained cdrom disks can take it from your fingers without
biting you.

   Now, if you want to print something on it first, try OpenOffice.org. They
have several label formats for cdrom already present. I use one of the Avery
numbers with the Office Depot labels.

> My OS is Fedora 3.

   That's OK. OO.o runs on it.

From pem at nellump.net  Tue Feb  1 12:45:05 2005
From: pem at nellump.net (Paul Mullen)
Date: Tue, 1 Feb 2005 12:45:05 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] MAC Mini running Linux?
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0501311742070.7108-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0501311742070.7108-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
Message-ID: <20050201204505.GA9719@nellump.net>

On Mon, Jan 31, 2005 at 05:59:22PM -0800, Roderick A. Anderson wrote:

> Anyone tried it yet or thinking of porting Linux to the mini-Mac?

Yes. Rumor has it the Mini Mac is not much more than a warmed-over
iBook G4. Differences include the power management and thermal control
silicon, among a few others that I don't recall. The lead kernel
developer for PowerMac systems makes it sound like there's no real
impediment (other than the usual lack of documentation) to getting a
fully-supported Linux install up and running on the Mini.

Some local guy ordered a Mini with the intention of installing Linux
on it, and journaled his experience on a weblog. He gave up,
unsatisfied with the lack of support for some features. It'll just
take time.

<http://krussell.com/mini/>


Paul



From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Feb  1 12:54:18 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 1 Feb 2005 12:54:18 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: Red Hat ? How to find a file on a CDROM 
In-Reply-To: <20050201200015.3A31559D7@ulke.nakedape.cc>
References: <20050201200015.3A31559D7@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <20050201205418.GA8863@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Tue, 1 Feb 2005, Norm Coder wrote:
> I have been asked to install a couple program from the Red Hat WS3 CDROM.
> When I ran a find -name 'tcl-devel*' on each CD and came up with nothing.
> Then I realized the files I was looking for must be embedded in an .rpm
> file. My first question is where would I find the following files? Is
> there a way to search for them on the CD other than what I did? I also
> know I should be able to install these programs using System Settings,
> Add/Remove Applications. In case that didn't work I wanted to know the
> other way using the rpm -ivh command.

When I load a new distro, I unpack all the iso's into a subdirectory
of my "spare" partition so I have a huge directory full of rpms.
(Probably I should just keep the iso's around and mount them in
loopback).  In any case, given the long string of rpms, either from
a directory or a mounted iso, I run a bash script that lists all the
iso contents and puts them into a text file for later searching.  The
core of the script does this:

   for  file  in  `find $dir -type f -print | grep rpm`
   do
      /bin/echo \
      "$iso $file ----------------------------------" \
                             >> $OUT
      /bin/rpm -qilp $file   >> $OUT
      /bin/echo ""           >> $OUT
   done

If I ever get the motivation to it right, I would build three
scripts, the first that loops through and mounts and unmounts
 all the iso's in a distribution to make the big long list. 
The second script greps through this file for a particular
string, and lists the rpms that contain it. A third script,
given the rpm, mounts the iso containing the rpm and loads 
the rpm.  A fourth script might be a cheesy kind of "yum",
that not only loads an rpm but all it's dependencies in the
appropriate order.

But I am too lazy, and that kind of setup is useful enough that
you would think someone would already have written it.   I am 
too lazy to even go hunting for it at sourceforge or whatever.

Keith

From rlucas at tercent.com  Tue Feb  1 13:22:55 2005
From: rlucas at tercent.com (Randall Lucas)
Date: Tue, 01 Feb 2005 13:22:55 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: debian on dell inspiron 1100
Message-ID: <41FFF32F.4040706@tercent.com>

I had trouble with Debian X on some Dells with (IIRC) the i810 onboard 
video.  My fix was to go into the BIOS and change the video memory from 
1 MB to 8 MB -- this is a crappy onboard video card that uses system 
memory.  Also, you should look for the "Debian on Dells" project hosted 
at Oregon State for kernels and even install CDs with kernels suited to 
recent Dell hardware.

Good luck, and enjoy Debian!

Randall

From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Tue Feb  1 13:30:41 2005
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Tue, 1 Feb 2005 21:30:41 +0000 (UTC)
Subject: [PLUG] Re: Red Hat ? How to find a file on a CDROM
References: <20050201200015.3A31559D7@ulke.nakedape.cc>
	<20050201205418.GA8863@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <slrncvvsgp.a6b.wcooley@rheingold.nakedape.priv>

On 2005-02-01, Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> wrote:
>
> When I load a new distro, I unpack all the iso's into a subdirectory
> of my "spare" partition so I have a huge directory full of rpms.
> (Probably I should just keep the iso's around and mount them in
> loopback).

Yes, you should :)

I create an /etc/autofs.isos and use autofs to mount the ISOs on demand.
Then I use 'lndir' from the X11 distribution to make symlinks to the files
in the auto-mounted ISOs.  That, along with the 'symlinks' tool, allows
me to maintain a sizable symlink-farm.  The only downside is that I cannot
simply NFS-mount the link farm and have everything work without also mounting
the ISOs over the network.  (Which is mainly a problem when trying to do
network installs.)

Wil

# The following was supposedly scribed by
# Wil Cooley
# on Tuesday 01 February 2005 03:30 pm:

>?The only downside is that I cannot
>simply NFS-mount the link farm and have everything work without also
> mounting the ISOs over the network. ?(Which is mainly a problem
> when trying to do network installs.)

Ah, but you can use samba if you configure it without unix extensions 
and "follow symlinks".  A good trick for making programs under wine 
play-nice with symlinked directories btw (though autocad still does 
that silly copy/overwrite thing that kills symlinked files and/or any 
groups/permissions that you might have set.)

Now, can you mount your own samba share and export that via nfs?

I've been using similar strategies for my subversion repository 
check-outs.  Wish I would have know about lndir before I wrote 
hop_to_links (though I may have still done it just to have control 
over what doesn't get linked.)

http://ericwilhelm.homeip.net/svn/Module-Subversion-Juggle/trunk/data/notes/how_this_works.txt

http://ericwilhelm.homeip.net/svn/Module-Subversion-Juggle/trunk/data/scripts/

I've been using these scripts to do the "live install" of my various 
perl/python modules and scripts, but it works for any files (and I've 
recently been playing with it for pictures, etc.)

--Eric

> -p <foo> is the preparer ID. Something like "this awesome disk prepared by 
> Bill's lackey on 2-1-2005." This also can have a default in .mkisofsrc, 
> PREP=<foo>. Command-line overrides the defaults.
> 
> man mkisofs tells all.

Thanks. Believe it or not, I tried "-V" and  I got an error in cdrecord.
So I removed it and cdrecord worked.  Probably a typo that went
unnoticed.
> 
-- 
Bill Spears <bspears at easystreet.com>

On Tue, 2005-02-01 at 09:37 -0800, Norm Coder wrote:
> I have been asked to install a couple program from the Red Hat WS3 CDROM.
> When I ran a find -name 'tcl-devel*' on each CD and came up with nothing.

> file. My first question is where would I find the following files? Is there

Try

You did not give it a path.  That should find it.

On Tue, 2005-02-01 at 10:20 -0800, Rich Shepard wrote:
> On Tue, 1 Feb 2005, Norm Coder wrote:
> 
> > I have been asked to install a couple program from the Red Hat WS3 CDROM.
> > When I ran a find -name 'tcl-devel*' on each CD and came up with nothing.

> Norm,
> 
>     I'm no longer running Red Hat here so I don't have 'man rpm'. But, the
> syntax is something like
>   	rpm -q --what provides <file_name>

Actually, the syntax in Red Hat Enterprise Linux is specific to the
distro:

rpm --redhatprovides /path/to/filename

It requires that you have the rpmdb-redhat RPM installed. Wildcards are
possible if you have the right path.

Mike

From ron at braithwaites.net  Wed Feb  2 08:32:11 2005

In-Reply-To: <1107359123.29180.20.camel@apollo.spears.org>

Message-ID: <1107361931.6398.7.camel@hermes.braithwaites.net>

On Wed, 2005-02-02 at 07:45 -0800, Bill Spears wrote:
> I need to mount a usb film reader on Fedora 3 system. Here's what we
> know:
> 1. Yesterday it worked automatically. When I plugged the USB cable into
> the computer, an icon appeared, much like a CDROM icon and I was able to
> access the media thru that. Today nothing.
> 2. I tried "mount -t vfat /dev/sda1 ~me/camera_film/" and it replied
> "mount: special device /dev/sda1 does not exist".  I also tried sdai for
> i=2...4.
> 
> What else can I try?

I'm familiar with this problem. Seems the /dev/sda1 device doesn't
"exist" when you just plug in the camera. On startup, kudzu (or
whatever) discovers the camera (and/or other USB devices) and assigns
it/them to /dev/sda1..n 

Apparently, if the device is not plugged in and turned on when your
computer is rebooted, the device is never discovered.

I would *LOVE* to change that behavior. Suggestions would be
appreciated.

-Ron

From ron at braithwaites.net  Wed Feb  2 08:37:13 2005
From: ron at braithwaites.net (Ron Braithwaite)
Date: Wed, 02 Feb 2005 08:37:13 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Microsoft's Ten Immutable Laws of Security
Message-ID: <1107362233.6398.10.camel@hermes.braithwaites.net>

This was on the SANS list this morning. As much as I hate to give any
credit to M$, these "laws" are pretty good. Of course, they weren't
quite complete, so the SANS editors made some changes to make them more
inclusive. Which goes to show that even when M$ does something right, it
is generally a day late and a dollar short.

-Ron

***

Microsoft's Ten Immutable Laws of Security

Please provide examples of real security incidents that illustrate any
of these laws.  Other examples of security breaches caused by sysadmins
errors are equally welcome. Email them to info at sans.org Subject: 10Laws
(Original source and more details:
http://www.microsoft.com/technet/archive/community/columns/security/essays/10imlaws.mspx}

We've made a few changes [in brackets] to make them a little more
inclusive.

Law #1: If a bad guy can persuade you to run his program on your
computer, it's not your computer anymore

Law #2: If a bad guy can alter the operating system on your computer,
it's not your computer anymore

Law #3: If a bad guy has unrestricted physical access to your computer,
[or data] it's not your computer anymore

Law #4: If you allow a bad guy to upload programs to your website, it's
not your website any more

Law #5: Weak [or weakly protected] passwords trump strong security

Law #6: A computer is only as secure as the administrator is trustworthy
[and is aware of threats and countermeasures]

Law #7: Encrypted data is only as secure as the decryption key

Law #8: An out of date virus scanner is only marginally better than no
virus scanner at all

Law #9: Absolute anonymity isn't practical, in real life or on the Web

Law #10: Technology is not a panacea

Law 1 example
A sysadmin at one e-commerce company received an email that looked like
a security alert and contained a url that seemed to go to Microsoft for
patches. He clicked on the hyperlink, taking him to the fake Microsoft
site. He downloaded the fake patch and infected his system with a
keystroke logger that recorded his passwords and account names for every
system to which he had access. More than a dozen of the servers he
managed were later used by the attackers as pornography servers.

Law 5 example
A sysadmin for an aerospace contractor posted sensitive Department of
Defense files on a computer in the DMZ that also had a configuration
weakness.  The files were stolen and a major DoD investigation ensued.

We look forward to receiving your examples.

-- 
Ron Braithwaite
Technical Consulting Services
ron at braithwaites.net
+01-503-267-3250
4110 SE Hawthorne Blvd #228, Portland, OR 97214 USA
1917 W 4th Ave #549, Vancouver, B.C. V6J 1M7 Canada

From griffint at pobox.com  Wed Feb  2 08:42:43 2005
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Wed, 2 Feb 2005 08:42:43 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] USB mounting
In-Reply-To: <1107359123.29180.20.camel@apollo.spears.org>
References: <1107359123.29180.20.camel@apollo.spears.org>
Message-ID: <20050202164243.GA11525@aracnet.com>

On Wed, Feb 02, 2005 at 07:45:23AM -0800, Bill Spears wrote:
> I need to mount a usb film reader on Fedora 3 system. Here's what we
> know:
> 1. Yesterday it worked automatically. When I plugged the USB cable into
> the computer, an icon appeared, much like a CDROM icon and I was able to
> access the media thru that. Today nothing.
> 2. I tried "mount -t vfat /dev/sda1 ~me/camera_film/" and it replied
> "mount: special device /dev/sda1 does not exist".  I also tried sdai for
> i=2...4.
> 
> What else can I try?
> -- 
> Bill Spears <bspears at easystreet.com>
> 

Some PCs have a chronic problem with this. One of my legacy computers
is an old 400Mz Celeron and it's real fussy about re-plugging in USB 
devices. It's definitly a hardware problem, maybe in the BIOS or in
the USB adapter. The only fix for that particular PC is to shut it down
and remove AC power to force the hardware to completely reinitialize. If
I just reboot, that's not enough. I've seen these sorts of problems less 
frequently in newer computers.

Watch your /var/log/messages file when you plug the device in. This
should give some clues. Sometimes the device will be assigned to /dev/sdb
(or some other /dev/sd*) instead of /dev/sda. If so this will be shown in 
/var/log/messages.

Terry

From ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net  Wed Feb  2 10:22:08 2005
From: ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Wed, 2 Feb 2005 12:22:08 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] USB mounting
In-Reply-To: <1107359123.29180.20.camel@apollo.spears.org>
References: <1107359123.29180.20.camel@apollo.spears.org>
Message-ID: <200502021222.08135.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>

# The following was supposedly scribed by
# Bill Spears
# on Wednesday 02 February 2005 09:45 am:

>I need to mount a usb film reader on Fedora 3 system. Here's what we
>know:
>1. Yesterday it worked automatically. When I plugged the USB cable
> into the computer, an icon appeared, much like a CDROM icon and I
> was able to access the media thru that. Today nothing.
>2. I tried "mount -t vfat /dev/sda1 ~me/camera_film/" and it replied
>"mount: special device /dev/sda1 does not exist". ?I also tried sdai
> for i=2...4.

Are you using udev? (not sure if that matters)

With my smartmedia reader, I have to unplug the device and plug it 
back in (with the card in it) after I umount it.  You might find 
that /dev/sda exists, but not /dev/sda1.

The device getting plugged-in triggers a kernel event, but changing 
the card doesn't, so the partition goes away.  Aside from physically 
plugging the device, the following two commands (issued by root) get 
the partition to appear again.

  fdisk -l /dev/sda
  blockdev --rereadpt /dev/sda

--Eric

That was sufficiently interesting that I'm going to report what
happened:
(dmesg told me:
 Attached scsi removable disk sdb at scsi3, channel 0, id 0, lun 0
USB Mass Storage device found at 7)
/sbin/fdisk -l dev/sdb told me:
Disk /dev/sdb: 32 MB, 32768000 bytes
8 heads, 16 sectors/track, 500 cylinders
Units = cylinders of 128 * 512 = 65536 bytes

   Device Boot      Start         End      Blocks   Id  System
/dev/sdb1   *           1         500       31982+   1  FAT12
/sbin/blockdev --rereadpt /dev/sdb
returned no output
After that
 mount -t vfat /dev/sdb1 ~me/camera_film/
worked fine.

BTW, I'm pretty sure Fedora 3 uses udev and I thought it was supposed to
handle events like USB plugging and unplugging.  The log showed each
time that plugged and unplugged the USB, but as you said there was no
partition to mount.

Thanks to all.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Feb  2 10:58:21 2005

Carla Schroder wrote:
> Law #1: If a bad guy can persuade you to run his program on your
> computer, it's not your computer anymore
>
> Law #2: If a bad guy can alter the operating system on your computer,
> it's not your computer anymore
> 
> Wow, either the PLUG list has mellowed, or a big meteor hit Portland, or
> you're all laughing too hard to post. So let me be the first to say the
> blindingly obvious: "But the core, warp, woof, and fiber of the Windows
> architecture is to allow, indeed, to welcome these very things." No
> persuasion necessary, Windows always has the red carpet out for malware.

Think of it as a wordy version of the warnings they put on the side
of cigarette packs.  It is there to make consumers feel guilty, NOT
to change consumer behavior.  If consumers had the time and interest
to manage security on their computers, they would immediately notice
that (1) it is very hard to do under windows, and (2) it is much
easier to manage security with Linux or OS X.  

Microsoft plays on the guilt and fear of consumers;  like a spoiled
child whining at mommy,  they try to shame people into spending money
and ceding control.  Their whole message is "we are smart and you are
stupid, let us control you".  Unlike the common F/OSS message, "we are
smart and you are stupid, go away".  Microsoft will disappear in a
puff of greasy smoke when we change the F/OSS message to "you are
master of your computer, how can we help you?"  

Keith

From AthlonRob at axpr.net  Wed Feb  2 11:32:57 2005
From: AthlonRob at axpr.net (AthlonRob)
Date: Wed, 02 Feb 2005 11:32:57 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Bit-Torrent
In-Reply-To: <000501c50958$ad24a880$6400000a@gamma>
References: <000501c50958$ad24a880$6400000a@gamma>
Message-ID: <1107372777.7614.16.camel@dell.linux.box>

On Wed, 2005-02-02 at 10:54 -0800, Piet van Weel wrote:
> Does anybody here have a good experience with bit-torrent?
> I can NEVER get good transfer rates using it. Any ideas or suggestions?

Are you disabling uploads, perhaps?  That'll cut in to your download
rate significantly.  Look at the Seeder/Leacher ratio, as well... the
worse that ratio, the worse your transfers will be.

Generally the type of people utilizing the torrent will determine its
transfer rate.  If you download something like Law & Order: SVU for last
night because your cable went out for a half hour at 10:15, you'll
probably find not really great transfer rates because most people
downloading it are interested in getting the file, not sharing or
helping the community.

On the other hand, if you're trying to download a Slackware ISO, you'll
probably find much better speed, because the other people downloading it
are more likely to share their bandwidth to help a guy out.

-- 
Rob                    |  If not safe,
  http://rob.axpr.net  |    one can never be free.

From ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net  Wed Feb  2 11:47:03 2005
From: ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Wed, 2 Feb 2005 13:47:03 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] USB mounting
In-Reply-To: <1107370764.29180.31.camel@apollo.spears.org>
References: <1107359123.29180.20.camel@apollo.spears.org>
	<200502021222.08135.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>
	<1107370764.29180.31.camel@apollo.spears.org>
Message-ID: <200502021347.03978.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>

# The following was supposedly scribed by
# Bill Spears
# on Wednesday 02 February 2005 12:59 pm:

>/sbin/fdisk -l dev/sdb told me:
>/dev/sdb1 ? * ? ? ? ? ? 1 ? ? ? ? 500 ? ? ? 31982+ ? 1 ?FAT12

>/sbin/blockdev --rereadpt /dev/sdb
>returned no output

Sorry, I wasn't clear about the equivalent effect of those two 
commands.

Either one of them causes the partition table to get re-read.  The 
list (-l) option to fdisk will, of course, list the partition table.  
This apparently requires that the kernel first reread the partition 
table, so what you want is just that side-effect.

If you aren't interested in viewing the partition table, the blockdev 
command gets you the desired effect by itself (and AFAIK returns no 
output.)

--Eric

-----Original Message-----
From: plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org
[mailto:plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org] On Behalf Of AthlonRob
Sent: Wednesday, February 02, 2005 11:33 AM
To: General Linux discussion and assistance
Subject: Re: [PLUG] Bit-Torrent

On Wed, 2005-02-02 at 10:54 -0800, Piet van Weel wrote:
> Does anybody here have a good experience with bit-torrent?
> I can NEVER get good transfer rates using it. Any ideas or
suggestions?

Are you disabling uploads, perhaps?  That'll cut in to your download
rate significantly.  Look at the Seeder/Leacher ratio, as well... the
worse that ratio, the worse your transfers will be.

Generally the type of people utilizing the torrent will determine its
transfer rate.  If you download something like Law & Order: SVU for last
night because your cable went out for a half hour at 10:15, you'll
probably find not really great transfer rates because most people
downloading it are interested in getting the file, not sharing or
helping the community.

On the other hand, if you're trying to download a Slackware ISO, you'll
probably find much better speed, because the other people downloading it
are more likely to share their bandwidth to help a guy out.

--

From mike at mommabears.com  Wed Feb  2 14:13:28 2005
From: mike at mommabears.com (MJang)

Subject: [PLUG] Red Hat ? How to find a file on a CDROM
In-Reply-To: <420133D8.2040709@paranoid.org>
References: <75D481373A76D311A5790090274F2B5C05C02F28@mailsrv1.gemstone.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.61.0502011017520.11837@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<1107358245.6961.17.camel@suse1>  <420133D8.2040709@paranoid.org>
Message-ID: <1107382408.13986.22.camel@suse1>

On Wed, 2005-02-02 at 12:11 -0800, Rich Burroughs wrote:
> MJang wrote:
> 
> > Actually, the syntax in Red Hat Enterprise Linux is specific to the
> > distro:
> > 
> > rpm --redhatprovides /path/to/filename
> 
> Ok, I didn't know that (never used RHEL), but it's really goofy. Why 
> would they change the options to RPM? Especially after all of the 
> time/energy over the years spent promoting RPM as a standard that should 
> be adopted by others.

It's certainly not the first goofy thing Red Hat has done. But the
--redhatprovides switch is linked to their database of files and
packages (rpmdb-redhat, as mentioned previously). The file doesn't have
to be installed for --redhatprovides to work, as long as you cite the
right path. Naturally, it wouldn't work with other distros. So there's
some justification for a distro specific switch. 

I think rpm -qf /path/to/filename works on all rpm-based distros, as
long as the associated package is installed.

Thanks,
Mike

From 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com  Wed Feb  2 14:42:36 2005
From: 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com (Steve Bonds)

On Wed, 2 Feb 2005 08:03:15 -0800, Norm Coder wrote:

> Rich, I am using RH WS3 (2.4.21-27.0.2) I like your idea and would like to
> use yum. Where can I find it? I googled "yum linux" and received a plethora
> of cool information, but none that jumps out with a clear path forward.
> Thanks in advance

The best source for YUM on Red Hat Enterprise and clones is:

http://dag.wieers.com/home-made/apt/

Dag coordinates with FreshRPMs and other RPM sites to ensure that
they're all internally consistent.  He offers really simple
instructions on getting YUM set up here:

http://dag.wieers.com/home-made/apt/FAQ.php#B3

I often have problems with the "$releasever" variable and instead
hardcode in a "3", as in:

----- sample yum.conf entry -----
[dag]
  name=Dag RPM Repository for Red Hat Enterprise Linux
  baseurl=http://apt.sw.be/redhat/el3/en/$basearch/dag
-----

  -- Steve

>From message of Wednesday 02 February 2005 12:12:
: Does anybody here have a good experience with bit-torrent?
: I can NEVER get good transfer rates using it. Any ideas or suggestions?
:
: I have found over time that a lot of it has to do with the client.  The
: best client I have found is BitComet.  I am using under windows and don't

I am having a great time in Linux (F3) and using Azureus.
Great, easy-to-understand GUI, installs with a double-click, and you can tune 
u/l & d/l rates, no. of connections, etc. to balance your loar or prioritize 
incoming files, seeding, etc. Basically, as a user NOT interested in 
programming, if even *I* can be happy with it, then the program is pretty 
much ready for prime time.

Don't forget to put total caps on aggregate U/L & D/L so as to leave you a 
little headroom for browsing & e-mails.

From rsteff.l at comcast.net  Thu Feb  3 07:29:35 2005
From: rsteff.l at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Thu, 3 Feb 2005 07:29:35 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Resolved: php and where mpg123 lives
Message-ID: <200502030729.35142.rsteff.l@comcast.net>

Some long time ago, a couple of years, I think, I posted my music database 
(php and mpg123) project on my web site. Yesterday, I got an e-mail from a 
fellow in Massachusetts who is working on something similar and found my 
code! (My few moments of coding fame?) He was having a problem getting mpg123 
to work from php. He could run things like ls, but not mpg123.

I got the e-mail just before I had to go out, so I responded with the short 
answer that I vaguely recalled a problem with permissions, and that I'd check 
further when I got home.

I got an e-mail from him this morning that said my comment reminded him to 
look where the programs live. Apparently, php can't see some directories. On 
his machine, mpg123 lived in /usr/local/bin. Programs like ls live 
in /usr/bin. Once he moved mpg123 to /usr/bin, php had no problem with it.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens
http://home.comcast.net/~rsteff/

From rich at paranoid.org  Thu Feb  3 11:00:25 2005
From: rich at paranoid.org (Rich Burroughs)
Date: Thu, 03 Feb 2005 11:00:25 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: Resolved: php and where mpg123 lives
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0502030923440.25227@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <200502030729.35142.rsteff.l@comcast.net>	<Pine.LNX.4.61.0502030827080.11795@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>	<slrnd04lfv.a6b.wcooley@rheingold.nakedape.priv>
	<Pine.LNX.4.61.0502030923440.25227@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <420274C9.8060405@paranoid.org>

Rich Shepard wrote:

>   A chroot jail, eh? So, not to flog a deceased equine, but is there a
> security difference in allowing executables to run from /usr/bin but not
> /usr/local/bin?

There is a big difference between those two directories when you think 
about the FHS and what is installed where.

/usr/bin:

http://www.pathname.com/fhs/pub/fhs-2.3.html#USRBINMOSTUSERCOMMANDS

/usr/local/bin:

http://www.pathname.com/fhs/pub/fhs-2.3.html#USRLOCALLOCALHIERARCHY

The things in /usr/local/bin are all installed by the local admin and 
they do not come with the distribution.


Rich

On Thu, Feb 03, 2005 at 12:01:24PM -0800, Russ Johnson wrote:
> AthlonRob wrote:
> 
> >Limit your upload rates if you're on DSL.  Or shape your traffic if
> >you're so inclined - on DSL, if you upload full blast, your download
> >(and latency) will suffer greatly.
> > 
> >
> OK, I'm confused.
> 
> As I understand it, DSL uses different frequency ranges for upload and 
> download, and they shouldn't interfere with each other. So in theory, 
> upload speed and download speed should not impact each other.

What happens is that if you max out the upload or download speed, data
backs up in the modem's queue, causing a kind of gridlock that slows
things waaay down.  So you cap UL/DL rates just below the maximum to
prevent this.


From heinlein at madboa.com  Thu Feb  3 21:45:49 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Thu, 3 Feb 2005 21:45:49 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] WYSIWYG HTML editor (redux.?)
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502021839200.20335-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502021839200.20335-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0502032138270.12827@pecos.madboa.com>

On Thu, 3 Feb 2005, Roderick A. Anderson wrote:

> They are creating a site in Spanish and though the editor ( I don't 
> know/care which one ) and web browser ( Firefox/Mozilla ) are 
> showing the correct letters when they come from the web server they 
> are question marks.

It's a question of the character set used to create the page is 
mismatched with the web server's default character set. The page is 
probably encoded via UTF-8, while the web server defaults to 
ISO-8859-1 -- though there's a small chance the situation is just the 
reverse of that.

Rather than having them resort to character entities, the best 
long-term fix is probably to get the web server in shape to serve up 
Unicode pages.

What web server software are they using? If Apache, check out the 
AddDefaultCharset and AddCharset directives.

-- Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

Perhaps this is a better solution: Ensure that your web server is using
the same charset in the HTTP headers and the document itself is using.
At least, that's what people are telling me, although I haven't entirely
sorted it out yet.

I'm sorta running into similar problems with some documents I'm
generating from DocBook. See http://nakedape.cc/info/Cyrus-IMAP-HOWTO.
You might notice odd characters that (on my Firefox at least) are
rendered as commas in the nagivation links at the top and bottom.  If I
manually change the charset to ISO-9660 or ASCII from UTF-8, the
characters are not displayed.  I don't seem to be the only one either; I
noticed it on the Samba docs pages too, although they seem to have
resolved it.

Wil

On Thu, 2005-02-03 at 12:01 -0800, Russ Johnson wrote:
> OK, I'm confused.

After reading your email, so am I....

> As I understand it, DSL uses different frequency ranges for upload and 
> download, and they shouldn't interfere with each other. So in theory, 
> upload speed and download speed should not impact each other.

If it's like that, then something else must be seriously wrong with a
lot of DSL.

> It's not like a modem that has to transmit and receive over the same 
> voice spectrum. It's more like transmitting on channel 14 and receiving 
> on channel 15 on your CB. Of course, the other end is transmitting on 
> channel 15 and receiving on channel 14.

>From personal experience, I can either upload at full capacity or
download at full capacity, but never both at the same time.  Download
speed cuts in to upload speed a but, but upload speed cuts in to
download speed drastically, and when uploading things, latency goes to
hell in a handbasket (making ssh unusable it's so bad).

Some time ago I began investigating traffic shaping to better share my
resources via BitTorrent (for things like Slackware ISOs and such)... I
never actually implemented anything, but a common thread I seemed to see
in people's comments regarding traffic shaping uses was to solve this
upload-kills-the-connection problem so many DSL users seem to have.

I can't offer anything more than anecdotal evidence that this is the
case... so take it for what it's worth.  :-)

From aaron at bavariati.org  Fri Feb  4 00:33:12 2005

On Thu, Feb 03, 2005 at 05:05:01PM -0800, AthlonRob wrote:
> Some time ago I began investigating traffic shaping to better share my
> resources via BitTorrent (for things like Slackware ISOs and such)... I
> never actually implemented anything, but a common thread I seemed to see
> in people's comments regarding traffic shaping uses was to solve this
> upload-kills-the-connection problem so many DSL users seem to have.

Indeed.  And it's the same with cable internet.

I used the the Wondershaper script to cap bandwidth on my home box
and it did, well, wonders.  The Debian version has improvments (it
accepts command-line arguments and comes with an excellent quickstart
in README.Debian) so I'd suggest using that one.  If you don't run
Debian, use Alien to convert it to the package format of your choice.

With it in place and tuned, I can hammer my connection up and down and
still have responsive SSH and decent WWW.  I'm thinking of adding some
settings to prioritize SIP traffic, but no need for that yet.

Tuning's easy: you ping your next-hop (Qwest's router, say), start
a big FTP download, and slowly turn the download bandwidth up 'til
your ping times go bad.  Back off a little and that's your DL number.
Then you do the same thing with an upload.

All the cool kids are doing it,
  Aaron ;)

From heinlein at madboa.com  Fri Feb  4 07:28:11 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Fri, 4 Feb 2005 07:28:11 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Re: WYSIWYG HTML editor (redux.?)
In-Reply-To: <slrnd0638e.31g.wcooley@rheingold.nakedape.priv>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502021839200.20335-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
	<slrnd0638e.31g.wcooley@rheingold.nakedape.priv>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.62.0502040703330.2386@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Fri, 4 Feb 2005, Wil Cooley wrote:

> Perhaps this is a better solution: Ensure that your web server is 
> using the same charset in the HTTP headers and the document itself 
> is using. At least, that's what people are telling me, although I 
> haven't entirely sorted it out yet.

My bias is toward moving all my web pages to UTF-8, so here's what I 
did...

First, I made sure that the DocBook stylesheets produced UTF-8 output. 
I did that by writing a custom wrapper around the default xhtml 
stylesheet:

<xsl:stylesheet
      version='1.0'
      xmlns:xsl="http://www.w3.org/1999/XSL/Transform"
      xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">

   <xsl:import
        href="/usr/share/sgml/docbook/xsl-stylesheets/xhtml/docbook.xsl"/>

   <xsl:output
        method="xml"
        encoding="UTF-8"
        indent="no"
        doctype-public="-//W3C//DTD XHTML 1.0 Transitional//EN"
        doctype-system="http://www.w3.org/TR/xhtml1/DTD/xhtml1-transitional.dtd"/>

   ...

</xsl:stylesheet>

Second, I set Apache up to serve UTF-8 by default:

    AddDefaultCharset UTF-8

So the files are Unicode-encoded and the web server lets clients know 
about it:

$ HEAD www.madboa.com
200 OK
Connection: close
Date: Fri, 04 Feb 2005 15:23:32 GMT
Accept-Ranges: bytes
ETag: "30624-fbc-b5c96680"
Server: Apache/2.0.48 (Linux/SuSE)
Content-Length: 4028
Content-Type: text/html; charset=UTF-8
...

Anyway, that's what works for me.

On the other hand, if you've got a bunch of UTF-8 files and you're 
pretty sure that you won't be able to convince the webmaster to serve 
them up correctly, you can use iconv(1) to do the conversion, e.g.,

   iconv -f UTF-8 -t ISO8859-1 page.html > page.new.html

--Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>


From galens at seitzassoc.com  Fri Feb  4 07:37:19 2005

AthlonRob <AthlonRob at axpr.net> wrote:

> On Thu, 2005-02-03 at 12:01 -0800, Russ Johnson wrote:
> > OK, I'm confused.
> 
> After reading your email, so am I....
> 
> > As I understand it, DSL uses different frequency ranges for upload and 
> > download, and they shouldn't interfere with each other. So in theory, 
> > upload speed and download speed should not impact each other.
> 
> If it's like that, then something else must be seriously wrong with a
> lot of DSL.
> 
> > It's not like a modem that has to transmit and receive over the same 
> > voice spectrum. It's more like transmitting on channel 14 and receiving 
> > on channel 15 on your CB. Of course, the other end is transmitting on 
> > channel 15 and receiving on channel 14.
> 
> From personal experience, I can either upload at full capacity or
> download at full capacity, but never both at the same time.  Download
> speed cuts in to upload speed a but, but upload speed cuts in to
> download speed drastically, and when uploading things, latency goes to
> hell in a handbasket (making ssh unusable it's so bad).

I wonder whether this can really be blamed on the DSL hardware.  I think
poor throughput in the un-traffic-shaped case may be due to high TCP ACK
latency.  It seems that this would be likely to happen with any TCP
connection with large buffers and a slow (relative to ethernet) bit
rate.  In this case, getting the TCP ACK packets sent in a timely manner
is certainly a software issue.

An interesting experiment would be two simultaneous UDP transfers.
Since UDP packets aren't ack'd, this should show whether the hardware
slows down when both directions are utilized.

galen

From heinlein at madboa.com  Fri Feb  4 08:16:50 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Fri, 4 Feb 2005 08:16:50 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Pine + mailcap + open on Mac OS X
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.62.0502040806340.2386@arrowhead.galois.com>

Here's some more fun with Pine on Mac OS X...

The osx build of pine doesn't include a default search path for 
mailcap, the little database that maps MIME types to applications, so 
pine doesn't know how to launch helper applications to view 
attachments.

The workaround, however, is pretty easy:

1. Modify .pinerc so that it knows how to find mailcap:

    mailcap-search-path=~/.mailcap

2. Create a simple ~/.mailcap file that essentially relies on open(1)
    and LaunchServices for all its MIME savvy:

    application/*; /usr/bin/open %s
    audio/*; /usr/bin/open %s
    image/*; /usr/bin/open %s
    video/*; /usr/bin/open %s

That does it. Pine is now able to launch attachments without any 
trouble.

I'm reluctant at this point to turn everything over to open, but 
perhaps someday my .mailcap will be a one-liner :-)

  */*; /usr/bin/open %s

--Paul "newbie browser? feh!" Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

with this software. There ain't no linux equivalent that's worth the effort
to convert all the data. And, it's proprietary software so there's no way to

that provides the best, IMO, solution: run everything you can on linux and
fire up a virtual Winduhs machine for the critical app that cannot be
replaced.

On 2/4/2005 7:37 AM, Galen Seitz wrote:
> I wonder whether this can really be blamed on the DSL hardware.  I think
> poor throughput in the un-traffic-shaped case may be due to high TCP ACK
> latency.  It seems that this would be likely to happen with any TCP
> connection with large buffers and a slow (relative to ethernet) bit
> rate.  In this case, getting the TCP ACK packets sent in a timely manner
> is certainly a software issue.
> 
> An interesting experiment would be two simultaneous UDP transfers.
> Since UDP packets aren't ack'd, this should show whether the hardware
> slows down when both directions are utilized.


Yes, this is likely the cause.
FreeBSD's ipfw has a way to prioritize ACKs that have little ot no payload, 
and this helps tremendously on cable. (of course, pf+altq can do it too)

I don't know if linux can do the same ... but its much better than throttling 
bandwidth all together!

http://www.topfx.com/prioritizingackfreebsd.shtml
http://www.benzedrine.cx/ackpri.html

-Charlie

> > rate.  In this case, getting the TCP ACK packets sent in a timely manner

> > slows down when both directions are utilized.

> 
> I don't know if linux can do the same ... but its much better than

From ehem at m5p.com  Fri Feb  4 14:29:17 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Fri, 4 Feb 2005 14:29:17 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Bit-Torrent
In-Reply-To: <20050204153931.75E2C58E3@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200502042229.j14MTHO2087227@m5p.com>

>From: Galen Seitz <galens at seitzassoc.com>
> I wonder whether this can really be blamed on the DSL hardware.  I think
> poor throughput in the un-traffic-shaped case may be due to high TCP ACK
> latency.  It seems that this would be likely to happen with any TCP
> connection with large buffers and a slow (relative to ethernet) bit
> rate.  In this case, getting the TCP ACK packets sent in a timely manner
> is certainly a software issue.

Possible, and a number of folks have suggested such a thing, but seems
strange to me. Notably TCP doesn't need a low RTT to work, and BitTorrent
doesn't care about latency at all only bandwidth.

The one bit of speculation that seems true is the observation that
because payload packets tend to be large, they crowd out the smaller ACK
packets in buffers. Depending on the buffering algorithm you end up, if
an ACK packet arrives first at your DSL/cable/modem box it gets into the
buffer and there is still room for a large packet so it will take a
payload packet if it arrives, if a payload packet arrives it will fill
the buffer to the point where it cannot accept a full packet so it will
drop anything that comes before it empties. This payload can follow ACK
but ACK cannot follow payload theory, might explain payload going through
and jamming the ACK packets. At least this is one theory I've seen, I'd
love for a network person to chime in and say this is or isn't true.

If the problem really is TCP ACKs, then traffic shaping could be very
effective. You don't so much want to limit upload, as ensure that ACK
packets get higher priority than payload packets. The easy way to
distinguish these would be to take packets smaller than 128 bytes (or so)
and give them higher priority.


--

From aarontc at gmail.com  Fri Feb  4 16:30:46 2005
From: aarontc at gmail.com (Aaron Ten Clay)
Date: Fri, 4 Feb 2005 16:30:46 -0800

In-Reply-To: <000501c50958$ad24a880$6400000a@gamma>
References: <000501c50958$ad24a880$6400000a@gamma>
Message-ID: <41f575d105020416304153c262@mail.gmail.com>

On Wed, 2 Feb 2005 10:54:51 -0800, Piet van Weel <pmvw at cablerocket.com> wrote:
> Greetings.
> 
> Does anybody here have a good experience with bit-torrent?
> I can NEVER get good transfer rates using it. Any ideas or suggestions?
> 
> Piet

I've downloaded the last couple releases of CentOS with BitTorrent
about as fast as my connection would allow (~700K/sec). The key, I
believe, is to have sufficient bandwidth for all the peer to peer
traffic, requesting pieces and such. I usually allocate about 50K/sec
up to get 700K down.

Also, if you're behind a firewall, it's very beneficial to forward
some ports to your system and tell your client which ports you have
available. The default ports are 6881-6889, if I remember correctly.

Aaron

the remaining three are gone.

From max.reid at saikonetworks.com  Sat Feb  5 10:15:19 2005
From: max.reid at saikonetworks.com (max.reid at saikonetworks.com)
Date: Sat,  5 Feb 2005 10:15:19 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Samba vs nfs
In-Reply-To: <1107622927.9299.8.camel@itchy.crisponions.com>
References: <1107622927.9299.8.camel@itchy.crisponions.com>
Message-ID: <1107627319.42050d3781b79@webmail.no-ip.com>

Quoting David Phillips <redhat at crisponions.com>:

> I recently built a share on my linux server that I am sharing with
> windows machines via samba.  I would also like to share this share with
> my linux machines as well.  Problem is, if I mount the share via smbfs
> it only allows read/execute access to users and only root has write
> permissions, windows clients can write to the share without problems.  I
> need my linux users to be able to write to this share as well.
> 
> What I was wondering if it is possible to share a folder using 2
> different methods.  From my server can I share the folder via samba and
> also share the folder to my linux machines using nfs, or will I risk
> possible data corruption.

The problem with multiprotocol filesharing has to do with the differences 
between locking mechanisms in NFS and CIFS when two users are accessing the 
same file simultaneously using the different protocols.  If your kernel and 
samba implementation supports CIFS opportunistic locking, you shouldn't have 
this problem...

This feature has been available for some time on proprietary systems like 
Netapp Filers and some commericial *nix implementations for some time, so it's 
pretty mature and fairly common practice these days.

Regards,
Max

research last night I discovered that the M2444 were once connected to
Sun boxes with these Xylogics 472 cards (which weren't SCSI, therefore
must have been Pertec) using an xt (as opposed to st) device.

A Sun box interface would have the nice feature that it would be
easily network accessible and thus I could get access to the tape that
way.

From fpikus at gmail.com  Sat Feb  5 21:13:17 2005
From: fpikus at gmail.com (Fedor Pikus)

Subject: [PLUG] Samba vs nfs

References: <1107622927.9299.8.camel@itchy.crisponions.com>
	<1107627319.42050d3781b79@webmail.no-ip.com>

On Sat,  5 Feb 2005 10:15:19 -0800, max.reid at saikonetworks.com
<max.reid at saikonetworks.com> wrote:
> Quoting David Phillips <redhat at crisponions.com>:
> 
> > I recently built a share on my linux server that I am sharing with
> > windows machines via samba.  I would also like to share this share with
> > my linux machines as well.  Problem is, if I mount the share via smbfs
> > it only allows read/execute access to users and only root has write
> > permissions, windows clients can write to the share without problems.  I
> > need my linux users to be able to write to this share as well.
> >
> > What I was wondering if it is possible to share a folder using 2
> > different methods.  From my server can I share the folder via samba and
> > also share the folder to my linux machines using nfs, or will I risk
> > possible data corruption.
> 
> The problem with multiprotocol filesharing has to do with the differences
> between locking mechanisms in NFS and CIFS when two users are accessing the
> same file simultaneously using the different protocols.  If your kernel and
> samba implementation supports CIFS opportunistic locking, you shouldn't have
> this problem...
> 

In theory, yes. In practice, if users are accessing same files
simultaneously, locking is unreliable even with one protocol, and it's
not just linux nfs issue, I've seen very flaky nfs behaviour on
solaris and hpux as well. Basically, once you have a heterogeneous
environment, if your file locking seems reliable, you haven't stressed
the servers enough. They will start giving intermittent errors under
load. So you basically have to accept that you're taking chances if
you are support concurrent accesses.

-- 
Fedor G Pikus (fpikus at gmail.com)
http://www.pikus.net
http://wild-light.com


From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Sun Feb  6 01:29:58 2005

On 2005-02-06, Evan Heidtmann <clydefrog at adnap.no-ip.com> wrote:
>

> I know my uses are low-traffic, but I'm not sure how low. I'd like to

> http, etc. How can I keep track of how much bandwidth I'm using and how
> it's being used?
>
> When I move to paid hosting, I'll be living with a hard cap of per-month
> transferred data. What can I do to cripple my system or throttle it down
> when I get near the cap?

Probably none at all.  You'd be surprised by how little traffic you actually
generate.  With the handful of sites I host on my DSL pipe, including the
PLUG mailing lists and web site and a number of other lists and sites,
my actual traffic is rarely over a couple hundred kilobytes per second.

See the graph[1] from IPCop of my last month of traffic.  The blue represents
outbound traffic and the green in-bound.  The higher-traffic blue is from
me running a couple of torrents of CentOS and SuSE ISOs; compare that with
the other times when I'm not running torrents.

You'll see occasional in-bound spikes; these are from downloading things
like the latest CentOS 3.4 updates and such.

1. http://haus.nakedape.cc/~wcooley/xfer/RED-month.png

Wil

Hi Fedor,

Agreed, there are certain risks. NFS locking is more of an after thought in many
environments, and samba doesn't exactly have deep integration with the
underlying unix filesystem, however for light or moderate use, its a lot less
expensive than doubling disk or using seperate fileservers.   Also, keep in mind
that Microsoft essentially permits you to do the same thing if you are running
the NFS service on their fileserver product... and I personally have had fewer 
issues with the penguin/samba(or CIFS)/nfs combo than the windows/CIFS/NFS combo.

If the server is going to be heavily loaded enough to break things and/or
mission critical enough where having an occasional borked file is not an option,
then it might be easier to justify the disk overhead, seperate server or a
commerical product like a Netapp filer or EMC NAS box. 

Regards,
Max

From jason at vancleve.com  Sun Feb  6 13:01:58 2005
From: jason at vancleve.com (Jason Van Cleve)
Date: Sun, 6 Feb 2005 13:01:58 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] user add problem
In-Reply-To: <200502062026.j16KQ3A74805@pop.hevanet.com>

Message-ID: <20050206130158.575d3b4a.jason@vancleve.com>

Quoth William A Morita, on Sun, 6 Feb 2005 12:26:01 -0800:

> The uid is created. E.g. in /etc/passwd along with a home directory,
> but I cannot log into the account.

Did you run passwd for the new account, as root?  You will need to
define a password before you can log in.

If you have, I'm guessing there's a problem with your login scripts,
/etc/profile, /etc/bashrc, ~/.bash_profile, ~/.bashrc (maybe something
from /etc/skel/).  Try commenting things in those files.

Also, make sure the default shell is /bin/bash, in /etc/passwd, unless
you specified another shell.

--Jason

From ehem at m5p.com  Sun Feb  6 13:15:11 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Sun, 6 Feb 2005 13:15:11 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Software for dealing with bandwidth limits?
In-Reply-To: <20050206200014.9418651E2@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200502062115.j16LFB9o095415@m5p.com>

>From: Evan Heidtmann <clydefrog at adnap.no-ip.com>
> I know my uses are low-traffic, but I'm not sure how low. I'd like to
> know how many bytes per month are transferred with SSH, with smtp, with
> http, etc. How can I keep track of how much bandwidth I'm using and how
> it's being used?

iptables and ifconfig.

One of the numbers provided by running `ifconfig` on an interface are the
counters for traffic in, and out. Won't include everything, notably I
don't believe the entirety of the ethernet frame is accounted for,
however this does give you a good outline.

Sounds like iptables is more what you want. iptables includes counters
for both byte count and packet count processed by every rule. Simply make
a rule that matches packets to/from the particular port pointing at the
ACCEPT target. Packets to/from that port will be included in the count
for that rule, but will not be included in the count for the next rule.

> When I move to paid hosting, I'll be living with a hard cap of per-month
> transferred data. What can I do to cripple my system or throttle it down
> when I get near the cap?

Traffic shaping.

Designate high, medium and low bandwidth points. Once you've exhausted
the high bandwidth point, slow things down a notch; once you're past the
medium point, slow things down another notch. Ad nauseum.

I'm not sure what part of the man page you mean. I do see this:

"If you need to delete a remote file you can try the rm command. Much of 
the time this won't work because you won't have the proper access

That's just saying you need the rights to delete the file or it won't

simple protocol.

What did the ownership and the permissions on the directory look like?

problem involving ownership/permissions without those kind of specifics.

From alex at daniloff.com  Mon Feb  7 09:42:15 2005
From: alex at daniloff.com (Alex Daniloff)

Subject: [PLUG] Two default gateways?
Message-ID: <20050207174215.GB15709@loki.dsl-only.net>

Hello Linux folkz,
Is it possible to have two default gateways
for the each host on internal network?
How to setup them?

I have the following network topology:
1. DSL modem connected to the switch_1
2. Two servers SW1 and SW2 with their own separate Internet
static IP's connected to the switch_1 via eth0 interfaces.
3. Two servers SW1 and SW2 with their own internal static IP's
but the same mask 255.255.255.0 and network address 192.168.1.0/24
connected to another internal switch_2 via eth1 interfaces.
4. The rest of the hosts on internal network connected to the switch_2
via their single eth0 interfaces.

What I want to achieve is to specify two default gateways for the each
host on internal network.
In case if SW1 or SW2 server goes down, each host still will be able
to access
the Internet.

Could somebody please enlighten me on this issue.
Many thanks in advance,

Alex


From srau at rauhaus.org  Mon Feb  7 10:19:54 2005
From: srau at rauhaus.org (Stafford A. Rau)
Date: Mon, 7 Feb 2005 10:19:54 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Two default gateways?
In-Reply-To: <20050207174215.GB15709@loki.dsl-only.net>
References: <20050207174215.GB15709@loki.dsl-only.net>
Message-ID: <20050207181954.GD20112@rauhaus.org>

* Alex Daniloff <alex at daniloff.com> [050207 09:45]:
> 
> What I want to achieve is to specify two default gateways for the each
> host on internal network.
> In case if SW1 or SW2 server goes down, each host still will be able
> to access
> the Internet.

Your problem there is going to be that your internal hosts have no
mechanism to mark the failed gateway host as being down. They'll either
continue to load balance between the two gateways, and half your traffic
will be dropped, or they'll pick one of the two gateways for all of
their traffic, and continue to send all of it to that one even if it
goes down.

You could look into using VRRP for linux - if you can get that working,
your two gateway machines will each have a "real" internal ip address,
such as 192.168.1.2 and 192.168.1.3, and they will have an election so
that one of them will always respond to a virtual ip, such as
192.168.1.1.

You would then point just a single default on your internal hosts at the
virtual ip, 192.168.1.1. When one of your gateway hosts goes down, the
VRRP process informs the other one to take over the virtual ip address.

I've never done this with linux, but did get some Google hits with VRRP
and linux. This a very common configuration with dedicated router
hardware, like Ciscos using HSRP or (now that they support it) VRRP.

--Stafford

Should have added that you could also use Zebra or GateD to run OSPF
on all of your hosts, and advertise a default route from each of your
gateway machines.

From max.reid at saikonetworks.com  Mon Feb  7 10:35:25 2005
From: max.reid at saikonetworks.com (max.reid at saikonetworks.com)
Date: Mon,  7 Feb 2005 10:35:25 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Two default gateways?

References: <20050207174215.GB15709@loki.dsl-only.net>
Message-ID: <1107801325.4207b4edd61fd@webmail.no-ip.com>



Hi Alex,

I'm assuming this setup is for redundancy and not necessarily loadbalancing, so 
if I'm incorrect in my assumption please let me know.

I would first suggest a better option: would it be possible to run VRRP/CARP on 
the two linux gateway server?   This would eliminate the problem all together, 
as both servers can represent a single (or multiple) virtual routers to the 
client  machines.

If that is not an option:

If the clients are Windows 2000 or XP, i believe you can specify multiple 
default gateways (under the NIC configuration---> TCP/IP ---> Advanced)... ON 
linux, you can run a routing protocol on the gateway servers and client (RIPv2 
is the most common) and loopbacked aliases or iproute with policy routing 
enabled in the kernel of the client machine.  


Regards,
Max



Quoting Alex Daniloff <alex at daniloff.com>:

> Hello Linux folkz,
> Is it possible to have two default gateways
> for the each host on internal network?
> How to setup them?
> 
> I have the following network topology:
> 1. DSL modem connected to the switch_1
> 2. Two servers SW1 and SW2 with their own separate Internet
> static IP's connected to the switch_1 via eth0 interfaces.
> 3. Two servers SW1 and SW2 with their own internal static IP's
> but the same mask 255.255.255.0 and network address 192.168.1.0/24
> connected to another internal switch_2 via eth1 interfaces.
> 4. The rest of the hosts on internal network connected to the switch_2
> via their single eth0 interfaces.
> 
> What I want to achieve is to specify two default gateways for the each
> host on internal network.
> In case if SW1 or SW2 server goes down, each host still will be able
> to access
> the Internet.

From fpikus at gmail.com  Mon Feb  7 09:56:33 2005
From: fpikus at gmail.com (Fedor Pikus)

Subject: [PLUG] Two default gateways?
In-Reply-To: <20050207174215.GB15709@loki.dsl-only.net>
References: <20050207174215.GB15709@loki.dsl-only.net>
Message-ID: <a4fbdc7b050207095678023c53@mail.gmail.com>

On Mon, 7 Feb 2005 09:42:15 -0800, Alex Daniloff <alex at daniloff.com> wrote:
> Hello Linux folkz,
> Is it possible to have two default gateways
> for the each host on internal network?

No, there can be only one default route. You can set up another route
overlapping the default one and give it a higher hop count using
"Metric" option to the route command. But that does not solve the
problem of failover, your connection will keep trying to use the
default route.

What you need goes beyond the capabilities of Linux kernel routing,
you need additional software like Zebra:

http://www-106.ibm.com/developerworks/linux/library/l-emu/

> How to setup them?
> 
> I have the following network topology:
> 1. DSL modem connected to the switch_1
> 2. Two servers SW1 and SW2 with their own separate Internet
> static IP's connected to the switch_1 via eth0 interfaces.
> 3. Two servers SW1 and SW2 with their own internal static IP's
> but the same mask 255.255.255.0 and network address 192.168.1.0/24
> connected to another internal switch_2 via eth1 interfaces.
> 4. The rest of the hosts on internal network connected to the switch_2
> via their single eth0 interfaces.
> 
> What I want to achieve is to specify two default gateways for the each
> host on internal network.
> In case if SW1 or SW2 server goes down, each host still will be able
> to access
> the Internet.
> 
> Could somebody please enlighten me on this issue.
> Many thanks in advance,
> 
> Alex

Even if you can get failover on your gateways (which seems tractable),
you'll also have the problem that each gateway machine is going to
have it's own idea of NAT conntrack state.  Any open connections
through the machine that goes away will die.

I've played with the wordnet dictionary a little bit, and at one point 
was working on a random sentence constructor in perl.  Does that 
count?

How much sense do they need to make?

A cerebral tibetan mastiff could slosh thievishly after an cream puff.
An archducal thievery were officiate daily except the soursop tree.
The mini terrain was abye unpatriotically along an aftercare.
An longed-for hind end to be stag injuriously on an bean beetle.
An loverly stand oil would get behind peacefully under a 
psittaciformes.

The articles, verb tenses, etc still need work, and I'm a long ways 
from anything very conversational, but it does occasionally turn out 
some memorable phrases.

Another thought would be to grab a pile of texts from the Guttenberg 
project and randomly pull sentence fragments out of those, but maybe 
those would make too much sense.   Playing around with some simple 
grep and using perl to strip/randomize gives some real stinkers, but 
there's not a lot of science in that 10 minute experiment.

andbiddythe
theagedhadall
andknockedat
clearspaceof

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Mon Feb  7 13:57:51 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Mon, 7 Feb 2005 13:57:51 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: Cleaning up a website
In-Reply-To: <20050207190622.BB18751F1@ulke.nakedape.cc>
References: <20050207190622.BB18751F1@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <20050207215751.GA15668@gate.kl-ic.com>

Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> writes:
>    If it would not be a major hassle for me, I would like to offer to redo
> their site using xhtml and css. But, I don't know how much of a hassle it
> might be, whether there are SSI available (e.g., for submittal of abstracts,
> changing one's membership information and other interactive functions), or
> if it's worth even trying. I doubt very strongly that the ISP (which seems
> to be a computer shop offering e-mail and web hosting services on the side)
> would consider a F/OSS solution.
> 
>    My question to those of you with experience in a heterogeneous OS
> environment with web servers is whether or not it would be practical to
> offer long-distance assistance given the architecture involved.

One of the great things about the web is that an HTML link can go from
an "uptight site" to another that provides the capabilities necessary.
If their ISP is wierd, and they don't want to move everything, then
simply move the few troublesome interactive pages to another (F/OSS)
server, perhaps under control of the actual individual that deals
with the data.  Over time, migrate the site page by page.  There is
no need to put everything in one place.

I wouldn't want to keep critical data on a site that ran M$ 
insecure-ware, anyway.  The downside is that for proper SSL
certs, somebody will have to pay some money.

Lots of professional organizations divide up the tasks this way.
Often, when there is money involved for example, they use specialized
professional sites that are set up for this.


Keith

From raanders at acm.org  Mon Feb  7 16:28:23 2005
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Mon, 7 Feb 2005 16:28:23 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] The solution to World Domination
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502071603330.19670-100000@main.cyber-office.net>

After a particularly "interesting" session with a user I have determined
the solution to "World Domination".  All personal computer and Internet
users will have to be licensed.  This will require that they take a test 
of minimal computer use competency.
   It would consist of questions like:

      What is the difference between a right and left click of the 
mouse?  Left-handers that have reconfigured their mouse get extra credit.  
( Heck they should pass. )

      Where is the start button?

      Which socket in the modem does the wall "line" plug into? ( plus
three points if they can find their modem -- minus 10 points for selecting
the Ethernet socket )

      Where/what is the desktop?

      What are all those funny little pictures on the desktop called?

So we knock out ( in a fit of kindness ) 75% of the computer users.  Then
20% ( or whatever is left over ) convert to Linux, MAC, BSD, or other UNIX
when Microsoft goes out of business.

World Domination!

I'm sure this has been proposed before but it is a pretty harmless way to
vent on a Monday!

Thanks for allowing me to spread these bits and bytes.  You've been a 
wonderful audience.


Rod

     "Build A Brighter Lamp :: Linux Apache {middleware} PostgreSQL"

From fpikus at gmail.com  Tue Feb  8 15:16:50 2005
From: fpikus at gmail.com (Fedor Pikus)
Date: Tue, 8 Feb 2005 15:16:50 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Keeping the undo stack in VIM
In-Reply-To: <4209443E.2020902@tercent.com>
References: <4209443E.2020902@tercent.com>
Message-ID: <a4fbdc7b05020815163350fb8@mail.gmail.com>

On Tue, 08 Feb 2005 14:59:10 -0800, Randall Lucas <rlucas at tercent.com> wrote:
> As a follow-up, is it possible to maintain the undo stack between
> invocations? 

No. viminfo file is where you store persistent data between invocations.
You can save lots of things in viminfo, but undo stack is not one of
them. do ":h viminfo" from vim to read the help file.

Fedor G Pikus (fpikus at gmail.com)
http://www.pikus.net
http://wild-light.com


From 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com  Tue Feb  8 15:58:50 2005
From: 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com (Steve Bonds)
Date: Tue, 8 Feb 2005 15:58:50 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] SNMP Agent CPU Hog + Timeouts
Message-ID: <6877-94934@sneakemail.com>

PLUGgers:

I just set up SNMP monitoring for some of our older Red Hat Enterprise
2.1 systems using the RedHat-provided ucd-snmp-4.2.5-8.AS21.4.  The
snmpd process chews up a LOT of CPU time immediately after it gets its
first request, so much so that queries time out.  This is despite my
attempt at a really, really basic configuration:

----- snmpd.conf -----
####
# First, map the community name "mycommunity" into a "security name"

#       sec.name  source          community
com2sec notConfigUser  default       mycommunity

####
# Second, map the security name into a group name:

#       groupName      securityModel securityName
group   notConfigGroup v1           notConfigUser

####
# Third, create a view for us to let the group have rights to:

#       name           incl/excl     subtree         mask(optional)
view    systemview     included      system.sysDescr
view    systemview     included      system.sysObjectID
view    systemview     included      system.sysContact
view    systemview     included      system.sysName
view    systemview     included      system.sysLocation
view    systemview     included      system.sysUpTime
view    systemview     included      interfaces.ifTable
view    systemview     included      ip.ipAddrTable

####
# Finally, grant the group read-only access to the systemview view.

#       group          context sec.model sec.level prefix read   write  notif
access  notConfigGroup ""      any       noauth    exact  systemview none none

syslocation Data Center
syscontact UNIX Admins
------

A system call trace of the snmp agent when it's wedged (strace -p
<PID>) shows that it's strobing through /proc and RPM contents of the
host.  There's no access to that data, so there's no need to collect
it.  I may want to enable disk monitoring, so I don't want to use the
snmpd.conf directive "ignoredisk".

So far, both Google and the Net-SNMP website have failed me:

http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&lr=&q=net-snmp+snmpd+high+cpu
http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&lr=&q=net-snmp+snmpd+%2Fproc
http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&lr=&q=net-snmp+snmpd+timeout
http://www.net-snmp.org/docs/man/snmpd.conf.html

How can I turn off the time-consuming and CPU-consuming data collections?

  -- Steve

Subject: [PLUG] IPTABLES...
Message-ID: <1107913565.42096b5d8f08a@xerxes.robinson-west.com>



For

      iptables -A PREROUTING -t nat -i eth0 -p udp \

               -j REDIRECT --to-port 8081

I somehow want to replace -d ! $some_ip with
     -d ! $some_ip -d ! $a_second_ip ... -d ! $a_nth_ip

I get an error that there can't be multiple destinations.
Can I do this with &&?  For reasons I have
yet to figure out, I can't get to http://distance.pcc.edu/ 
through a proxy.  There are also other places I can't get
to through proxy.  I'd like to cut holes instead of 
bypassing the proxy altogether, unless there's a way in
squid to change the access method for 
http://distance.pcc.edu/ and other sites I currently can't 
access through it.

I sent an e-mail to Comcast asking their help regarding deleting a directory 
while logged in using ftp. They sent a lengthly reply in which they explain 
that FTP is the most common way sites are maintained on Comcast, but that the 
only client they "support" is the one you can invoke from a DOS command 
window in Winders. I tried it, and had the same problem: I can't delete a 
directory logged in via ftp. They did not address the question of the changed 
user name.

Another thing they mentioned was:

> You can access your File Locker in Internet Explorer by going to
> ftp://username:password at upload.comcast.net
> where username is your e-mail address without the @comcast.net part and 
> password is your password for e-mail. Then the FTP window will work like
> a file folder. Just drag the files into the folder that you want to 
> upload. 

I tried that from Konqueror, but I didn't include my password. No problem, I 
got a dialog that asked for it. I had the usual view Konqueror gives of a 
directory and files. I was able to delete the testDir directory I had created 
with ncftp. This will be much simpler than using another ftp client, so 
that's why, even though I did not solve the problem of deleting a directory 
with ncftp, I consider the issue resolved.

Thanks for all the suggestions.

From aaron at bavariati.org  Wed Feb  9 10:20:32 2005
From: aaron at bavariati.org (Aaron Burt)
Date: Wed, 9 Feb 2005 10:20:32 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Airport Extreme question
In-Reply-To: <1107821958.6365.3.camel@hermes.braithwaites.net>
References: <1107821958.6365.3.camel@hermes.braithwaites.net>
Message-ID: <20050209182032.GC13837@bavariati.org>

On Mon, Feb 07, 2005 at 04:19:18PM -0800, Ron Braithwaite wrote:
> Well, I've finally gotten around to replacing the old wifi router with
> an Apple Airport Extreme. I have plugged a printer into the USB port and
> my wife and my son can easily print to it. I, however, cannot.

I was hoping someone more knowledgable would answer this.

I believe the printer is being announced using ZeroConf (Apple calls
it Rendezvous) AKA mDNS.  There's a full implementation out there
called Howl, and a simple lookup util called mdns-scan.  Look 'em up
on Freshmeat.net.

I don't know what printer protocol the thing uses, but I'll bet it
talks LPR.  Might be configurable on the setup webpage.

Keep us posted,
  Aaron

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Feb  9 18:28:25 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Wed, 9 Feb 2005 18:28:25 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] IEEE PACE Feb 22 PACE Meeting - Beaverton's Incubator
Message-ID: <20050210022825.GA8739@gate.kl-ic.com>

----- Forwarded message from Ed Perkins <ed.perkins at verizon.net> -----

INSTITUTE OF ELECTRICAL AND ELECTRONIC ENGINEERS (IEEE) OREGON SECTION
		PACE (PROFESSIONAL ACTIVITIES) MEETING 

TOPIC:	The Open Technology Business Center -- A New Resource for 
		Business Development in Oregon 
SPEAKER:	LaVonne Reimer, Executive Director
DATE:		Tuesday, February 22, 2005
TIME:		6:30 PM - 8:00 PM
		Doors open 6:00PM
LOCATION:	Oregon Graduate Institute(OGI), Wilson Center Main Dining
Room
		See directions below.
COST:		FREE and open to the public
REGISTRATION: See www.ieee-or.org/events for registration.
		or go to http://cpd.ogi.edu/class.asp?n=05-ieee-0222

This PACE meeting of the IEEE Oregon Section will inform you about the 
newly launched Open Technology Business Center in Beaverton.

Abstract:

The City of Beaverton has just launched its Open Technology Business 
center, and its executive Director LaVonne Reimer, will describe this 
exciting new initiative. The Open Technology Business Center, created 
with $1.2 Million from the city of Beaverton, is a first-of-its-kind 
facility dedicated to supporting the formation, funding and growth of 
new companies in the Open Technology sector. Programs include an Open 
Technology executive institute for advisors, educators, consultants and 
investors. Participating entrepreneurs will have unique access to 
industry thought leaders and domain experts. Qualified early-stage 
companies may locate in the center's facility through its 
"ventures-in-residence" program.

In a press release on the center's web site www.opentechcenter.com 
Executive Director Reimer stated that "the Center will bring together 
the best minds to analyze business implications of the Open Technology 
movement and conduct applied research to new business models. This 
distinctive support will enable Open Technology start-ups to play their 
important role in accelerating the adoption of Open Technology 
innovations and products worldwide."

In her talk Reimer will describe what the Open Technology Business 
Center means to both the broader open source/open technology movement as 
well as to new business creation in the Northwest technology industry.

Speaker Bio:

LaVonne Reimer has more than 20 years experience involving corporate 
strategy and facilitating entrepreneurial growth. Most recently, Reimer 
was founder and CEO of Cenquest, a Portland, Oregon-based technology 
company. In this role, Reimer worked with large university and corporate 
education and IT infrastructure to facilitate web-based distribution of 
higher education. As CEO of a venture-backed start-up in the technology 
sector, Reimer gained extensive experience in all aspects of 
entrepreneurship from funding and software development to marketing and 
strategic alliances. She is a frequent guest speaker in graduate 
capstone classes and seminars for entrepreneurs. 

Before starting Cenquest, Reimer practiced law and taught as an adjunct 
professor at OGI School of Science and Engineering at OHSU and 
Northwestern School of Law at Lewis & Clark, also consulting to regional 
high-tech companies in the areas of business law and ethics. As in-house 
corporate counsel at Tektronix, Reimer managed business litigation and 
internal strategic initiatives including spin-offs, mergers and 
acquisitions. Prior to her years at Tektronix, she was a trial and 
appellate lawyer with the law firm of Ater, Wynne, a firm specializing 
in corporate, venture law and labor and employment matters. Reimer is a 
graduate of Hastings College of Law and Willamette University. 

Directions to Oregon Graduate Institute (OGI):

The meeting will be held in the main dining room of the Wilson 
Clark Center on the campus of the Oregon Graduate Institute of 
Science and Technology, 20000 NW Walker Rd., Beaverton, 
OR 97006 (503) 748-1121. See http://www.ogi.edu/maps/ for a campus map.
The Wilson Clark Center is Building #3 on the OGI Campus Map.

To get to OGI (Oregon Graduate Institute), from Portland, take Highway 
26 west, take Exit 64 (185th) and proceed south (left) on 185th. 
Continue on 185th to Walker Rd. Turn west (right) on Walker Rd. OGI 
is at the top of the hill on the left. Turn left onto Von Neumann Drive, 
parking is available in the lot. Wilson Center is opposite the parking area.

For further information on the program, contact Ed Perkins at
503-612-9397 or e.perkins at ieee.org

To add or remove from this mailing list see www.ieee-or.org for access to
our email list manager.

	Personal Web Page

References: <200502051021.58714.rsteff.l@comcast.net>
	<867jlhcyox.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

On Wednesday 09 February 2005 3:00 pm, Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> On Wednesday 09 February 2005 11:37 am, Russell Senior wrote:
> > If Richard wants to find out why one works and the other doesn't,
> > ethereal might be just the ticket.  Capture both, and see what is
> > happening under the covers.

I installed ethereal, started a capture session, and then ran ncftp again. I 
went through the same process where I created a directory, testDir, and then 
tried to delete it, getting the same "you're not the owner" response. After 
quitting from ncftp, I connected through Konqueror and deleted the directory.

Looking through the captured information from ethereal, I discovered several 
things. First, I need to learn more about minimizing what ethereal is 
watching, or I have to shut down e-mail checking every minute! However, I was 
able to read through and find the place where ncftp sends the rm command to 
the ftp site, and the error message reply. Then I scanned down and found the 
place where Konqueror sends the command RMD and succeeds in deleting the 
directory. So, to see if I really learned something, I logged back in to the 
site using ncftp, created the directory once more, and deleted it with rmd.

Conclusion: Yes, I learned something useful--I now know how to delete a 
directory on a Comcast Personal Web Pages site with ncftp. But, I also 
learned that it is a lot easier to manage the site through Konqueror, so 
that's what I'll be using in the future.

Thanks again, Russ, for the reminder about ethereal.

From Steve.Daggett at fiserv.com  Thu Feb 10 09:22:54 2005
From: Steve.Daggett at fiserv.com (Daggett, Steve)
Date: Thu, 10 Feb 2005 09:22:54 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Really Resolved: ncftp - delete directory problem on
	C omcast Personal Web Page
Message-ID: <008A26A81DAD96489E7D4FCF259849982D4309@eft01ms01.eft.fiserv.net>

 
Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> 
> Looking through the captured information from ethereal, I 
> discovered several things. First, I need to learn more about 
> minimizing what ethereal is watching, or I have to shut down 
> e-mail checking every minute! 

  Ethereal uses two different filter syntaxes.

  The capture filter uses the filter syntax from tcpdump (pcaplib).  In your
case, the filter would be something like "host <ip addr>".  The capture
filter is entered in the "Capture Options" window when you start new
capture.  You can use "man tcpdump" to see the complete capture filter
syntax.

  The display filter syntax is unique to Ethereal and follows a completely
different format.  You can set the display filter by double clicking on a
display line or hand enter a filter at the bottom of the Ethereal window.  

Steve D...



From svanhoosen at yahoo.com  Thu Feb 10 16:07:35 2005
From: svanhoosen at yahoo.com (Scott Van Hoosen)
Date: Thu, 10 Feb 2005 16:07:35 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Samba vs nfs
In-Reply-To: <CC5738F2CE677746976EC06CBD6B9D98C7CC@toonces.crisponions.com>
Message-ID: <20050211000735.80281.qmail@web53609.mail.yahoo.com>

Sorry I'm late on this, been busy and haven't been keeping up. Anyway,
I have had this problem before. You need to use smbmount as a normal
user to mount the samba partitions and have read/write access.

First, you may have to change permissions on the relevant files to
allow a normal user to use smbmount, such as:

chmod 4755 /usr/bin/smbmnt
chmod 4755 /usr/bin/smbumount
chmod 755 /usr/bin/smbmount

Use the following syntax to mount them:

smbmount //server/share /mountpoint -o username=user%password

This should fix all your problems, and from now all your life will be
good and pleasant. :)

-Scott

interest in compromising a seldomly used program for a measly $500 or 
$1,000.

#!/bin/sh
