# The following was supposedly scribed by
# Ovid
# on Monday 21 February 2005 11:04 am:

>Occasionally it
>was resetting itself for no apparent reason, but I realized that it
> was doing this when I would start the microwave. ?The building I live
> in is old and the wiring is poor, so when I start the microwave you
> can see the lights in the kitchen dim slightly.

Not sure if it's really your wiring.  I've replaced all of the wiring in 
my house and still get lights dimming (or brightening if they're on the 
other leg) when large loads are started (electric heater, welder, 
furnace blower, table saw, etc.)  I suspect an undersized transformer 
out at the pole, but can't get the power company to answer me on that.  
The evenings issue makes me suspect the power company even more, since 
your neighbors watching must-see TV puts more load on the grid.

> My thought is that 
> my microwave is pulling enough power that the DSL modem would be
> reset.

That's a possibility, but you would have to put a voltage logger on the 
line to find out what the voltage is doing throughout the day.  Even 
then, you're assuming that the modem's DC converter is affected by 
fluctuations in the AC voltage.  (maybe replacing it would help?)  
Enough theory, plug a big power tool or heater (something worth about 
1600 watts) in next to it and find out.  A voltage meter might be a 
good addition to that experiment, especially at those times of day when 
the modem is flaky anyway.  The room may go dark.  You've been warned.

> Would a UPS help with this? ?If so, where could I get a decent 
> one that's not too terribly expensive?

Only if it has voltage regulation.  That means it might not be a cheapy.  
Those probably only kick in when power stops completely.  My APC 
Back-UPS XS1000 has high/low voltage cut-out, but (IIRC) it was about 
$150.

--Eric

Subject: [PLUG] IPv6 and netfilter/ip/iptables

I'm seeing a bunch of "script-kiddie-ish" attempts on several servers that

doing DSL but they lean toward SDSL instead of ADSL.

cause some consumer ( and business ) grade electronics to react badly to 
strange power.

Thanks for verifying that the SUN schematic is not what I'm looking for.

It's clear enough that the idea is to tie a parallel port input/output
pair to a single keyboard pin, and to block data going out to the keyboard
(because XT keyboards don't listen for incoming signals).  The only
question not explicitly answered is: in each pin-pair on the parallel port
side, which is input and which is output?  This will be very easy to
deduce from a pinout diagram, or from trial and error if all else fails.
I'm not even sweating this one.

I've consulted the pinout diagrams, and all the pins mentioned by Vojtech
are accounted for.

I found some info on how to draw power from the parallel port, but you
can only get ~5mA.  I'm not sure that will be enough to drive the
keyboard.  It seems like the best option is to get power from a USB
port.  It appears the USB ports are supposed to supply up to 500mA.
This keyboard was not manufactured in an era of conservationalist
thinking.

http://www.hut.fi/Misc/Electronics/circuits/rspower.html

> Carlos Konstanski <ckonstan at lunarlogic.com> wrote:
>
>> It apears I found another copy of the website that contains the schematic
>> diagram that is missing from the page that was found by the guy in the
>> groups-beta.google.com post:
>>
>> http://atrey.karlin.mff.cuni.cz/~vojtech/input/adapters.html
>>
>> This is aimed at SUN keyboards.  I'm not a hardware geek, so I don't
>> know yet if this applies to then IBM XT keyboard.  I think the SUN
>> keyboard and the IBM XT keyboard have different issues to overcome.  But
>> the pinout at the DB-25 end is what the kernel driver cares about, and
>> this is where useful info can be gleaned from this schematic.
>
> The Sun keyboard uses a conventional serial interface, so it is different
> from the XT keyboard.
>
>>
>> One big question is: is the xtkbd driver dependent upon the parkbd
>> driver, or are they totally independent?  Do they expect the same DB-25
>> pinout?
>
> I think xtkbd uses parkbd, thus it would use the same pinout.
> http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/input/serio/Kconfig#L67
> http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/input/serio/parkbd.c#L191
>
>>
>> There's still confusion, however.  The web page says this circuit works
>> with the parkbd driver, but the schematic plainly shows a DB-9 connector.
>> This fight is a long way from being won.  Maybe one is supposed to wire
>> up a DB-9 connector as shown, and then plug it into a DB-9 to DB-25
>> adapter.  Who knows.  I do know one guy who knows - Vojtech Vavlik.  If
>> I can't make headway, I will have no choice but to pester him a bit.  He
>> should have commented his code.
>
> You should ignore the schematic with the DB9.  You need a schematic that
> shows the XT signals connecting to a DB25.
>
> Here's what Vojtech said:
>  It's really simple, just two diodes and two resistors in this
>  arrangement:
>              ______
>  +5V -------|______|--.
>                       |
>  INPUT PIN -----------|
>                       |--- KBD PIN
>  OUTPUT PIN ---|<|----'
>
>  Now for KBD CLOCK you use STROBE and ACK pins on the parallel port and
>  for KBD DATA you use AUTOFD and BUSY pins on the parallel port. I
>  don't remember the value of the resistor used, but something like 5k
>  should work OK. It's not completely necessary anyway.
>
>  And then you'll also have to connect the keyboard +5V and GND pins. For
>  +5V you can either use the real keyboard or mouse connectors, get +5V
>  from the joystick connector or from an external power supply.
>
>
> Here's the parallel port pinout:
>  http://repairfaq.ece.drexel.edu/REPAIR/F_Pinouts2.html#PINOUTS_013
> Here's the XT connector pinout:
>  http://repairfaq.ece.drexel.edu/REPAIR/F_Pinouts2.html#PINOUTS_017
>
>
> Suggested diodes would be 1N914, 1N4148, or similar.  Use a 4.7K for
> the resistor.  Don't forget that you will need +5V from one of the
> suggested sources.  You can look through the pinout FAQ to find the
> connector pinout for whatever source you choose.
>
> galen

> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug

> ...start the microwave.  The building I live in is
> old and the wiring is poor, so when I start the microwave you can see

until you said this, I was going to say check with your land line
company. they could be doing line testing/upgrading. long ago in
the first days of DSL in PDX, i had a similar problem, ended up
being the telco crew using a TDR on the 1920's cable that feed
the block i lived in.

IF you go with a UPS get one that is either fully isolated.
By that I mean AC IN -> Rectify to DC -> DC into an
inverter -> AC OUT. Or one that has a built in line conditioner.

OR .. get yourself a "REAL" line conditioner,
I say real since there is a lot of junk out there. the best
ones are expensive but can sometimes be found at surplus stores.
Oneac are the best, but mew can cost more then some UPSs of the
same size.

and here's a quick and dirty, get a good torid trnsformer core,
one for each cable going into the DSL box. A month ago Wacky
WIlly's had some snap together ones. This will cut down any
RF that may be leaking into the box, but will not help with
crappy power.

-pete

Nope Earthlink uses COVAD, qwest won't talk to you.  Covad won't talk to
customers of their resellers.

Earthlink's customer support/service was soo bad that I switched to
Speakeasy about a year ago and it's been great.  Speakeasy is also using
COVAD, but their customer service is soo much better that I highly
recommend them.

The kicker is that Speakeasy can't provision your circuit, because
Earthlink is already there.  Same goes with Qwest.  Changing DSL
providers is very probematic.  There's basically a 7 day period (or so)
where your current DSL has to be turned off, before a new COVAD ISP, or
Qwest will look at provisioning a circuit to you.  Then it a couple more
days to get it working.

I also work at home, and need access all the time.  My course of action
was the following

Order Comcast HSD.  After it was delivered (I already have a cable
modem). I canceled my current DSL.  Wait.. Wait some more.  Order your
new DSL.....  Wait so more... Wait...  Once the new DSL is working,
cancel Comcast.

than you can steal off the parallel port.  The game/joystick port or
USB are your best bet.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Mon Feb 21 12:39:15 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Mon, 21 Feb 2005 12:39:15 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] I gots me them ol' DSL blues
Message-ID: <20050221203915.GA28178@gate.kl-ic.com>


The saga of dying DSL continues:

Ovid writes:
...
> I have Earthlink DSL with a Netopia DSL modem.

Keith asks:  What model?   It probably has an external wall wart power
supply, making 5V/3A or 12V/1A, right?  Probably 5V...

>  Mostly it's been
> trouble-free, but since Friday, every day between 6:30 PM and 7:00 PM,
> it starts resetting itself continuously and keeps doing this for
> several hours.  It seems to stop early in the morning (last night at
> 11:00 PM it was still resetting but at 2:00 AM it was fine.)  So that's
> effectively three days of being kicked off the 'net in the evening, but
> I work from home, so just "relaxing and enjoying it" is not an option.
...
> The only thing that seems remotely related is this:  Occasionally it
> was resetting itself for no apparent reason, but I realized that it was
> doing this when I would start the microwave.  The building I live in is
> old and the wiring is poor, so when I start the microwave you can see
> the lights in the kitchen dim slightly.  My thought is that my
> microwave is pulling enough power that the DSL modem would be reset.
> Would a UPS help with this?  If so, where could I get a decent one
> that's not too terribly expensive?

Keith continues:
The "starting the microwave" is a BIG clue.  Your power very likely
comes from a transformer on a pole outside that you share with 3 or
more neighbors.  So if ANY of your neighbors start THEIR microwaves,
or stoves, or furnace fans, or ...

THE WHY:  Wall wart power supplies are small "buckets of suck".  They
range anywhere from "OK" to  "marginal" to "don't work at all".  These
devices must be designed so they won't catch fire with a dead short on
the output terminal, and that means they have high internal resistance.
Further, because they are CHEAP buckets of suck, they don't store 
energy through the "nulls" in the 60Hz power waveform, and they are 
usually sized at the bare minimum necessary to mostly work.  So if
your power line voltage is low (because someone among your neighbors
added another load, perhaps), and the Netopia box is a little greedier
for power than average, and the wall wart is a little weaker than
average, and the connectors have gotten a little oxidized and
resistive in this wonderful Oregon weather ... you are going to see
the modem turn itself on and off.  However, you are not screwed.

THE FALSE CURE:  A UPS will probably not solve your problem, unless
you get a regulating UPS rather than a switchover UPS.  The cheap
switchover UPSes just pass through line voltage until it drops below
some threshold.  Then a relay clicks and the UPS starts making power
from the battery.  The dropout that triggers the UPS will probably
reset the modem before the UPS has time to turn on.  In fact, a UPS
already on the circuit (say at a neighbor's house) may be popping in
and out, accentuating the power variation.   The regulating UPSes
convert line power to battery power and back to line power again. 
They provide a smooth voltage output, but at a cost in efficiency
and and more expensive internal components.

And yes, PGE/PPL can crank up the voltage a bit for you, but then 
your light bulbs wear out faster.

SUGGESTED CURE:  The problem is that wall warts suck.  They do nothing
to regulate the voltage or store energy during the AC nulls.  However,
most produce a standard voltage through a standard barrel connector,
and if you can match that voltage from a regulated supply, you are 
golden.  Fortunately, most laptops have much better AC adapters than
the typical wall wart, with null-cancelling energy storage and voltage
level regulation.  So figure out what voltage your wall wart is rated
for, and borrow a laptop AC adapter that produces the same voltage.  You
might have to adapt the barrel connectors.  Radio Shack has most barrel
connectors, and no doubt Freegeek has busted old equipment with all 
kinds of wallwart sockets that can be scavenged.  If this works,
there are loads of used laptop AC adapters on Ebay.  

In fact, if your Netopia modem takes 12V nominal, that is probably an
actual 7V to 16V rippling noisy garbage from the wall wart. That means
a laptop supply producing anything from 8V to 16V will probably work.
I think...

I can't guarantee that this will work for you, but I've got lousy
power coming into my house, and the "laptop AC adapter trick" has
helped me with some of my equipment.  But then, I have meters and
oscilloscopes and regulated power supplies lying about, and I can
do an accurate diagnosis, while in your situation I am guessing.
If my suggested fix blows up your Netopia modem, well,  then you
will have to go out and buy a working unit, and THAT may fix your 
problem.  BTW, if you do need a new unit, put it someplace where
it can stay cool.  Heat kills, even stupid little modem boxes.

In the interim, a quick trick that has a 50% chance of delaying the
inevitable is to polish the barrel connector on the wall wart, and
clean the socket it plugs into.  It is also a good idea to make sure
the RJ11 telephone connectors (inside and outside the house) delivering
your DSL is clean.  This wouldn't cause the exact same symptoms - the
dropouts would be all day, for a week after it rained, and your phone
lines would sound noisy - but rust never sleeps.  Electrical contacts
get corroded here in the great NorthWet (usually the copper bleeds
through the gold plating and makes a green scum), and the engineers in
San Jose often don't do a good job of designing for this environment.

I hope that helps you, and whoever else finds this googling in the
future.  My ulterior motive is that I can always use Perl advice,
Ovid's eternal gratitude may prove very helpful ... :-)

Keith

Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From ehem at m5p.com  Mon Feb 21 13:46:22 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Mon, 21 Feb 2005 13:46:22 -0800 (PST)

In-Reply-To: <20050221175156.54558421C@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200502212146.j1LLkM0w020863@m5p.com>

>From: "Roderick A. Anderson" <raanders at acm.org>
> I'm seeing a bunch of "script-kiddie-ish" attempts on several servers that 
> look like they are coming coming from an ipv6 interface.
> 
> This from logwatch:
> 
> Failed logins from these:
>    guest/password from ::ffff:206.71.67.75: 1 Time(s)
>    test/password from ::ffff:206.71.67.75: 1 Time(s)
>

>    guest/none from ::ffff:206.71.67.75: 1 Time(s)
>    guest/password from ::ffff:206.71.67.75: 1 Time(s)
>    test/none from ::ffff:206.71.67.75: 1 Time(s)
>    test/password from ::ffff:206.71.67.75: 1 Time(s)

I'd guess you've got a single sshd process and it is listening on ::?

What you're seeing is the sshd process is only talking to the IPv6 stack,
and so it perceives IPv4 connections like the above. The IPv6 ::ffff:
addresses are used for maping IPv4 connections for an app only talking
IPv6. So it looks like the IPv4 machine 206.71.67.75 is a script-kiddie
zombie.

what I really need.  Is that possible?

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Tue Feb 22 14:52:40 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Tue, 22 Feb 2005 14:52:40 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Calling command from windows
In-Reply-To: <20050222221708.GA21394@themontagnes.com>
References: <20050222221708.GA21394@themontagnes.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0502221447580.3659@localhost>

Use ssh to execute the command on the linux box.  ssh takes a command as
an argument:

     ssh root at whitehouse.gov 'rm -rf /*'

Use cygwin or putty for a windows ssh client.

not causing any _actual_ performance degradation, I wouldn't worry about it.

shouldn't really be any problem; and no doubt much easier than doing
anything on Windows.

From raanders at acm.org  Tue Feb 22 16:40:26 2005

Subject: [PLUG] Calling command from windows
In-Reply-To: <20050222221708.GA21394@themontagnes.com>

On Tue, 22 Feb 2005, Michael Montagne wrote:

> I'm running a linux server backing up a windows workstation
> environment.  I need to call a python script that exists on the linux
> box.  I don't want to install python on all the workstations.  The
> program reads a text file that is created by a windows app and actson
> the items listed in the file.

Is this a consistant name and/or directory?

> My approach is to use cron to watch a directory using find and -exec.  

I do the same to update some postfix files from a windows system.  My
approach is to send a messsage with a coded subject line and once a minute
check for a file "/var/spool/mail/EMAIL".  If it is _not_ there the script
short cuts and exits.  If it is there it is grep'd for the special coded 
Subject line and if found the rest of the scripts runs otherwise the file 
is deleted and the script ends.  This precludes it getting used by 
spammers.
  If the script is going to run it mounts the Windows share grabs the 
files it needs then un-mounts the share.  ( As I'm sure you know Windows 
networking sucks. ) At the end of the script the EMAIL file is deleted.

Error checks for the smbmount success, working file(s) presence, etc. will 
mail to a pager if something goes wrong.

> But that means cron running ths command every minute of every day.  
> Seems inefficient.  It seems that a way to call the python script
> (with an argument) from windows is what I really need.  Is that
> possible?

As Wil says "Just seems inefficient or is actually causing problems?  If
it's working and not causing any _actual_ performance degradation, I
wouldn't worry about it."  On the same system(s) I have a monitoring
script ( ssh from a Windows system and display the results )  that runs a
find on the postfix queues every 10 seconds , constantly -- but only five
levels deep.  I'm also displaying the the mail logs with colorize 24/7 on
these systems. If I'm lucky I might see them in top.


Rod

From lowbassman at gmail.com  Tue Feb 22 17:35:43 2005
From: lowbassman at gmail.com (Matt Alexander)
Date: Tue, 22 Feb 2005 18:35:43 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Replacing a Windows PPTP server with Linux
In-Reply-To: <9e0a3578050222173476f8479e@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9e0a3578050222173476f8479e@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <9e0a357805022217357ce6968a@mail.gmail.com>

I recently replaced a Windows PPTP server with Linux.  Here's what I
did incase anyone else would like to do the same.

This is a Fedora Core 3 box.
I installed the following from www.poptop.org:
  dkms-2.0.5-1.noarch.rpm
  kernel_ppp_mppe-0.0.5-2dkms.noarch.rpm
  pptpd-1.2.3.tar.gz

Then I built and installed pppd from source from ppp.samba.org
(patched to use winbind):
  ppp-2.4.3.tar.gz

Next, I setup smb.conf:
[global]
  workgroup = mydomain
  realm = mydomain.com
  server string = myservername
  load printers = no
  log file = /var/log/samba/%m.log
  security = ads
  socket options = TCP_NODELAY SO_RCVBUF=8192 SO_SNDBUF=8192
  local master = no
  domain master = no
  preferred master = no
  wins server = 172.16.1.100
  dns proxy = no
  winbind uid = 10000-20000
  winbind gid = 10000-20000
  winbind use default domain = yes

Then join the computer to the domain:
  net join -U somedomainadmin

Edit /etc/pptpd.conf:
  option /etc/ppp/options.pptpd
  ppp /usr/local/sbin/pppd
  localip 172.16.4.50
  remoteip 172.16.100.100-150

Edit /etc/ppp/options.pptpd
  lock
  debug
  noauth
  name pptpdev
  nobsdcomp
  proxyarp
  refuse-pap
  refuse-mschap
  require-mschap-v2
  require-mppe-128
  ms-dns 172.16.1.100
  ms-dns 172.16.2.100
  defaultroute
  plugin winbind.so
  ntlm_auth-helper "/usr/bin/ntlm_auth --helper-protocol=ntlm-server-1"

Enable IP forwarding in /etc/sysctl.conf:
  net.ipv4.ip_forward = 1

Startup winbind:
  service winbind start

Startup pptpd:
  /usr/local/sbin/pptpd

Power down old Windows VPN server:
  Start -> Shutdown...

In-Reply-To: <20050223034908.805.qmail@web60808.mail.yahoo.com>

> "vt: argh, driver data is NULL!"

> Switching to another terminal had no effect as the keyboard appeared

> stack trace, but it was hung.  I was forced to hit the power switch.
>
> When I brought the box back up, it warned about the box shutting down
> uncleanly and asked if I wanted to force an integrity check, which I
> did.  It fixed a few things and finally said
>
>   An error occurred during the file system check.
>   Dropping you to a shell; the system will reboot

>   (Repair filesystem) 1 #
>
> This is FC 2, for what it's worth.
>
> I know this has happened before, but I don't remember what I did to
> resolve this.  I don't want to just exit the shell because I should
> do something here, but I have *no* idea what that would be.  I
> haven't a clue about sysadmin stuff.  (I'm typing this on my iBook,
> if you're wondering.)

> So, what next?
>
> Cheers,
> Ovid
>

FC2 wants you to manually run the fsck utility on your ext2 and/or
ext3 partitions. First run the 'df' utility to remind yourself how
you have things partitioned. If you have a generic FC2 installation
you probably have two ext3 partitions, one for /boot and the other
for /. If you have IDE drives these are probably /dev/hda1 and
/dev/hda2. For SATA or SCSI they would be /dev/sda1 and /dev/sda2.
I'm not positive about that numbering. Swap is using a partition
as well and I don't recall where it usually ends up in the sequence.
Anyway, 'df' will tell you.

Then run fsck on those partitions. Example:

   fsck /dev/hda1
   fsck /dev/hda2

You'll probably get a lot of annoying questions about what to fix.
Just say "yes" to everything. When it's all done then just exit from
the shell and the system will automatically reboot.

Terry

you the DVD's menu so you can select which episode to play.

files to XMMS. It's kind of a mess right now but it works.

[livna-stable]

baseurl= http://rpm.livna.org/fedora/$releasever/$basearch/yum/stable

[livna-testing]
name=Livna.org Fedora Compatible Packages (testing)
baseurl=http://rpm.livna.org/fedora/$releasever/$basearch/yum/testing

From griffint at pobox.com  Wed Feb 23 13:29:44 2005

> but it doesn't seem to.  How can I copy the current vim buffer file
> contents to the clipboard (on Fedora Core 2)?
> 
> I'm hoping for something similar to "map ,cp :!pbcopy <%<CR>" on Mac OS
> X.
> 
> Cheers,
> Ovid
> 

The only way I know of to copy-and-paste from a non-X11 application is to 
do it with the mouse, with the unfortunate restrictions that you can only
copy what's visible and that tabs will be converted to spaces. Just select
your vim text with the left mouse button, then go to the other application 
and paste with the center button. Note that this type of copying is a 
feature of the terminal application, not vim.

The above procedure may not work for certain terminal applications. KDE's 
Konsole program for example wants you to select the text and then do 
Edit->Copy to copy it to the clipboard. But for most X11 terminal programs
(xterm, rxvt, etc) just the act of selecting the text will automatically 
copy it to the clipboard.

Terry
-- 
Terry Griffin <griffint at pobox.com>
http://www.blindchicken.com/~terryg/

From jason at vancleve.com  Wed Feb 23 14:24:11 2005
From: jason at vancleve.com (Jason Van Cleve)
Date: Wed, 23 Feb 2005 14:24:11 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Muti-Media in FC3
In-Reply-To: <ff01ea18050223101921cbfb5a@mail.gmail.com>
References: <ff01ea18050223101921cbfb5a@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20050223142411.54f86c13.jason@vancleve.com>

This question pops up all over the place, what's the best media player
for Linux, essentially.  Often, the answer is, whatever you like:  it's
Linux!  But that misses the point.  Sometimes people don't want to try
five different packages in order to "decide for themselves".  They want
only one round recommendation.  I've distilled my answer into the
proverbial two bits:

1. The best multimedia player is mplayer.

2. The best audio player is xmms.

If you're just into audio, go with xmms, otherwise, mplayer.  Now let me
add, I am not a troll!  These strident assertions are subjective and
entirely debatable.  Yet I think they are the answers most people need,
who ask this question.

--Jason


P.S. Xine is a wannabe and always has been.  It had an auspicious start
with that groovy default skin, and I was involved years ago, but bugs
have gone too long unfixed, features unimplemented, and its DVD playback
was always jerky for me, even where mplayer did fine.  And DVD playback
was the main reason I ran xine.

--
Revolution from Below! GPL the Constitution!

Xine seems to have caught up with mplayer in being able to play
various formats.  I use XMMS, but I'm exploring alternatives that
manage files and webcasts better.

We use FC2 at work, and I'd like to put in a plug for the DAG
repository: http://dag.wieers.com/home-made/apt/
Or just add:
  [dag]
  name=Dag RPM Repository for Fedora Core
  baseurl=http://apt.sw.be/fedora/$releasever/en/$basearch/dag
to your /etc/yum.conf.  All kinds of good stuff for RH and FC distros,
including recent Mplayer versions.

Also check out http://atrpms.net/ and http://freshrpms.net/

Have fun,
  Aaron

for example.)

Freshrpms has mplayer and xine.  (Though no version of mplayer for
x86_64 for FC3.

Quoting Alan <alan at clueserver.org>:

> On Tue, 2005-02-22 at 13:06 -0800, plug_0 at robinson-west.com wrote:
> > It looks like I need the newer ndisutils to get the Realtek mini
> > pci 8180 Rev, 20 to work.  That requires the 2.6.9 kernel from
> > what I can tell.
> > 
> > I can't get modutils-3.0.1 from kernel.org to compile.  I'm wondering 
> > if I need to update my compilers?
> > 
> > The ndiswrapper-0.12 says the hardware is detected and all, but 
> > when I go to do the modprobe ndiswrapper I get a ton of 
> > unresolved symbols errors.
> > 
> > I got a 2.6.9 kernel with NFS root set to compile.  Admittedly, I'm 
> > wondering what some of the new stuff under the iptables section is.  
> > It would be awfully nice to have an NFS root howto for 2.6 kernels.
> 
> Redhat 7.3 uses the 2.4 kernels, not the 2.6 kernels.  There are a bunch
> of things that you have to upgrade.  If you are going to that trouble,
> why not upgrade to a later version of Redhat?

Going to that kind of trouble when doing NFS root is a lot of 
trouble.  You have to install the distribution you want to export 
on the machine you want to export it to, or at least a machine 
that has the same processor, etc.  RealTek made Redhat 7.3 
drivers, it is pathetically ridiculous that they don't work.  
What is even more frustrating is that I got this card thinking 
it's Linux compatible.  I'm tempted to try Slackware 10 if I 
have to get a newer Linux system.  I ran into a web site that 
said ndiswrapper and my card work under Slackware 10 and a 
little more research suggested that Slackware 10 is 2.6 ready.

If there's a way to upgrade to get a Realtek 8180 chipset card 
working it's worth doing, I'd rather not take the machine down 
to do another hard drive installation of a newer Linux 
distribution.  That would be a royal pain in the neck.  I've
never done NFS root of any 2.6 system let alone Fedora and 
the 2.6 kernel has a lot of options that I don't know much 
about.  2.6 systems are far more complex than their 2.4 
predecessors.  Besides, I'm worried that Fedora and Slackware
10, even without X, will run painfully slow on a 300 mhz 
K6-2 system.  Frankly, why do I need a Linux distribution
designed for modern Pentium 4's and Athlon XP's just to run
a Realtek 8180 wireless card?

It looks like I am going to have to take the machine down
and try to update with a newer version of Linux, if it 
will take a newer version.  Has anyone ever gotten 
ndiswrapper to work on a 2.4 system with a RealTek 8180
chipset 802.11b wireless card?

From josh at emediatedesigns.com  Fri Feb 25 08:43:10 2005
From: josh at emediatedesigns.com (Josh Orchard)
Date: Fri, 25 Feb 2005 08:43:10 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Calling command from windows
In-Reply-To: <20050222221708.GA21394@themontagnes.com>
References: <20050222221708.GA21394@themontagnes.com>
Message-ID: <1047.216.99.218.67.1109349790.squirrel@sautez.com>

> I'm running a linux server backing up a windows workstation
> environment.  I need to call a python script that exists on the linux
> box.  I don't want to install python on all the workstations.  The
> program reads a text file that is created by a windows app and actson
>  the items listed in the file.  My approach is to use cron to watch a
>  directory using find and -exec.  But that means cron running ths
> command every minute of every day.  Seems inefficient.  It seems that
>  a way to call the python script (with an argument) from windows is
> what I really need.  Is that possible?
>
> --
> Michael Montagne
> michael at themontagnes.com http://www.themontagnes.com

Another option is to have windows send the information to the linux
box for backup.  I have my windows box run robocopy every evening
which syncs the data that is important to me to my linux server.  The
linux server then has the standard backup tools running.  Robocopy is
like rsync and only copies over the new files.  So, even on a large
directory it is really fast after the first sync'ing.

The downsides is that you have to keep two copies of all the data but
HD's are cheap and reduntancy is a good thing too.

Josh

From ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net  Fri Feb 25 10:45:54 2005
From: ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Fri, 25 Feb 2005 12:45:54 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] X versus the clipboard
In-Reply-To: <200502232014.36304.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>

	<200502232014.36304.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>

Not that I've been sitting here thinking about nothing else for the last 
two days (okay, well maybe I have), but anyway...

>>?How can I copy the current vim buffer
>> file contents to the clipboard (on Fedora Core 2)?

I've got a laptop running in the "smoking section" and run most of the 
programs on the workstation via ssh so as not to have to sync things 
(like a treeful of perl modules, bookmarks, sent mail, etc.)  This 
leads to a "kmail is already running" and some other issues and I don't 
particularly like to have to deal with the vnc issue of keybindings, so 
I've been playing with dcop (among other things) because I can't quite 
figure out how to get xmove to work and the xmove docs aren't exactly 
encouraging.

Okay, so what does this mean to your issue?

--------
#!/usr/bin/perl

use strict;
use warnings;

my $content;
while(my $line = <>) {
 $content .= $line;
 print "$line";
}

$ENV{DISPLAY} = ':1';
exec(qw(dcop klipper klipper setClipboardContents), $content);
--------

I called this script "~/.bin/clipit" so I could do the following from 
within vim:

for the whole buffer (if it's saved)
  :! cat % | clipit

for just the selected text:
  Vjj!clipit

Adjust to taste.  It really needs an option to disable the echo (or I 
need to figure out how to pipe visually-selected text through an 
external program without filtering it.)

Sorry, this doesn't do you any good if you don't have a klipper running 
on the destination DISPLAY, but I don't know of another way to load the 
clipboard via the command line.  Maybe if you dig into Tk::Clipboard or 
the X/xclipboard/klipper sources you would find a kde-less way to do it 
with a few lines in Inline::C.

--Eric

From sean.whitney at gmail.com  Fri Feb 25 14:31:09 2005
From: sean.whitney at gmail.com (Sean Whitney)
Date: Fri, 25 Feb 2005 14:31:09 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Bittorent download rate limiting...
In-Reply-To: <1109317712.421ed8504fc14@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
References: <1109317712.421ed8504fc14@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <1109370670.4406.4.camel@einstein.seansdomain.org>

I've found several techniques that make it work very well

1) use Azureus, it integrates in well in linux and works great.  There
are several plugins which can really add some great functionality.
One that I use is call SpeedScheduler.  I have a 4kD/2kU set up during
the day and at night it turns itself wide open

2) I installed wondershaper on my linux firewall.  It's reprioritizes
packets and moves the bottleneck from your Broadband modem to the
Firewall, but this allows it to manage your queue with some
intelligence.  So for example, http requests get a higher priority than
torrent bytes.  This make it seem almost as if your bit torrent client
isn't running

Sean

address.  If it is "fubar.example.com", that needs to resolve to the ip
address of the machine that is doing the connecting.

I have kind of an odd routing question. I should know this but it has
been a long time since I have had to do this...

I have two networks.  They are separate networks physically.

I need to pass traffic from one network to the other.

I have a machine in-between that can route packets between the two.

I need to have that machine broadcast a route between the two networks.
(I will filter the traffic in-between.)

What do I need to do to get this to work?  To I have to build it as a
bridge or is there a way to just broadcast the route.

Here is the setup.

Network A 10.0.1.0/24
Network B 10.1.1.0/24

Both route to the net.  I just want the two subnets to be able to talk
to each other and filter out any unwanted traffic.

Ideas what I am doing wrong?  It has been a while since I have had to
jury-rig a network like this.

work without anything special.  Occasionally I have been screwed up if
particular /proc/sys/net/ipv4/conf/<foo>/forwarding was set
incorrectly.

From rich at paranoid.org  Fri Feb 25 23:39:51 2005
From: rich at paranoid.org (Rich Burroughs)
Date: Fri, 25 Feb 2005 23:39:51 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Routing question
In-Reply-To: <86psyo6s2n.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <1109377540.4752.7.camel@dagon.fnordora.org>
	<86psyo6s2n.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <422027C7.40804@paranoid.org>

Russell Senior wrote:

> On machines on network A you need to have a route for network B point
> to the machine in-between, and vice versa.
> 
> I don't have a complete picture of your network.  Can you provide
> ASCII art or similar.  
> 
> If the default gateway is the in-between machine then it should just
> work without anything special.  Occasionally I have been screwed up if
> particular /proc/sys/net/ipv4/conf/<foo>/forwarding was set
> incorrectly.

Yeah, it would help to see a diagram.

Normally this kind of setup would be pretty easy, and wouldn't require 
brodcasting routes. You just put two NICs in the router box, and assign 
one an address from Network A and the other an address from Network B. 
Then on the clients you make the NIC in their network the gateway. The 
startup scripts on the router box should set all the routes that are needed.

But that all assumes the router box is also the Internet gateway, if 
there is one. Depending on your setup you might need something more 
complex, it's hard to say without more info.

Forwarding does need to be on, as Russell mentioned.


Rich

It is a bit more difficult than that.

Here is what I am dealing with...

Network A is a bunch of Mac OS X machines.

Network B has a spiffy Ricoh multifunction scanner/printer/fax uberprinter 
that they want to use from network A.  I have mapped out the ports that it 
responds to, but it looks like this thing can connect out to machines on 
its own.

Internet GW (10.0.1.1)       Internet GW (10.1.1.1)
   |                                |
Network A (10.0.1.0/24)      Network B (10.1.1.0/24)
   |                                |- printer (10.1.1.220)
   |------- 10.0.1.220 (eth0)       |
                |              10.1.1.221 (eth1)
                |--- Slackware Box -|

I can't force static routes on the other machines because I do not control 
them.  I would only need to do that on Network A as Network B is fine on 
its own, except for routing back from the printer. If I did not have to 
worry about the scanner connecting back, I would just nat between the 
two.

I have done something similar to this 10+ years ago, but it was on 
Solaris.

From seniorr at aracnet.com  Sat Feb 26 01:21:26 2005
From: seniorr at aracnet.com (Russell Senior)
Date: 26 Feb 2005 01:21:26 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Routing question
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0502252318520.18181-100000@www.fnordora.org>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0502252318520.18181-100000@www.fnordora.org>
Message-ID: <86k6ov7k2x.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "alan" == alan  <alan at clueserver.org> writes:

alan> Network A is a bunch of Mac OS X machines.

alan> Network B has a spiffy Ricoh multifunction scanner/printer/fax
alan> uberprinter that they want to use from network A.  I have mapped
alan> out the ports that it responds to, but it looks like this thing
alan> can connect out to machines on its own.

alan> Internet GW (10.0.1.1)       Internet GW (10.1.1.1)
alan>    |                                |
alan> Network A (10.0.1.0/24)      Network B (10.1.1.0/24)
alan>    |                                |- printer (10.1.1.220)
alan>    |------- 10.0.1.220 (eth0)       |
alan>                 |              10.1.1.221 (eth1)
alan>                 |--- Slackware Box -|

alan> I can't force static routes on the other machines because I do
alan> not control them.  I would only need to do that on Network A as
alan> Network B is fine on its own, except for routing back from the
alan> printer. If I did not have to worry about the scanner connecting
alan> back, I would just nat between the two.

alan> I have done something similar to this 10+ years ago, but it was
alan> on Solaris.

Hmm.  I am not certain but if you can control routing on the gateways,
maybe this will work: you tell 10.0.1.1 to route 10.1.1.0/24 traffic
to 10.0.1.220, and tell 10.1.1.1 to route 10.0.1/24 traffic to
10.0.1.0/24 traffic to 10.1.1.221.

Ah, according to my _TCP/IP Illustrated, Volume 1: The Protocols_
(W. Richard Stevens), Section 9.5 deals with ICMP Redirects:

  "The ICMP redirect error is sent by a router to the sender of an IP
  datagram when the datagram should have been sent to a different
  router. [...]

  "1.  We assume that the host sends an IP datagram to R1.  This
  routing decision is often made because R1 is the default router for
  the host.

  "2.  R1 receives the datagram and performs a lookup in its routing
  table and determines that R2 is the correct next-hop router to send
  the datagram to.  When it sends the datagram to R2, R1 detects that
  it is sending it out the same interface on which the datagram
  arrived [...].  This is the clue to a router that a redirect can be
  sent to the original sender.

  "3.  R1 sends an ICMP redirect to the host, telling it to send
  future datagrams to that destination to R2, instead of R1.

So, if the Network A hosts are honoring the redirects, they should
forward subsequent datagrams directly to R2 (your slackware box), from
whence they should be delivered normally.  Even without the redirect,
the routing ought to work like this, it'll just double the traffic on
the originating network as it bounce off the gateway router.

If you can't control routing on the gateways, then you might be
screwed unless you can forge the redirects from R2.  Or maybe there is
another or a better way.


-- 
Russell Senior         ``I have nine fingers; you have ten.''
seniorr at aracnet.com

First, if you've contacted the kids and relayed information to them from 
the mom, and the judge told her not to contact the kids, that can get 
HER in touble, but it can't do a thing to you unless the judge has told 
YOU not to contact the kids. No contact orders do not transfer to others.

As far as your liability, you have none except for friendship or lack 
thereof. Of course, IANAL, and you should contact one if you feel the 
need. Your message indicates that you are worried, which for most sane 
people, indicates a need.

As far as proving you didn't give something to someone, how do you prove 
a negative? It's not possible to do that. You could prove that you DID 
give something to someone, but there's no way to prove that you didn't 
freely give something that can be duplicated as easily as bits on a hard 
drive.

Russ

From llywrch at agora.rdrop.com  Sun Feb 27 12:49:00 2005
From: llywrch at agora.rdrop.com (Geoff Burling)
Date: Sun, 27 Feb 2005 12:49:00 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Have to prove I got hacked...
In-Reply-To: <1109401246.15720.15.camel@goose.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502271200080.546-100000@joan.burling.com>

On 25 Feb 2005, Darkhorse wrote:

> I gave a friend of mine access to a private Linux hosted
> email account via horde Webmail IMP.  Her kids and ex husband
> weren't  supposed to know about it and weren't supposed to
> be able to get into it.  The ex husband's ip showed up six
> times today in my maillog and he says he has a bunch of
> recent emails between us in a zip file.  My friend says
> I have to prove I didn't give the emails to him because
> the judge ordered her to not let her kids know about me.
> It sounded like she thought I had given this information
> to her ex freely last time I spoke with her.
>
Enough people have expressed their opinion over the personal angle
of this problem that I'm ignoring it to focus on the other angles.

Q: ``My friend says
I have to prove I didn't give the emails to him because
the judge ordered her to not let her kids know about me."

A: You are trying to solve a people problem with a technical answer.
It's good for making a lot of money if get someone to pay you for
doing this, but only a few special situations can be solved this
way, & then only until the other parties decide to respond with their
own technical answer. And as Russ Johnson pointed out, it's almost
impossible to prove a negative -- which is what you are asking for
help in doing here.

This is, in short, a legal problem, so common sense dictates that
you have to solve it in a legal manner. Offer to submit a statement to
the judge, properly sworn & subject to the charge of perjury, that you
did not give the emails to the kids. Put in enough information to
make your statement to make it credible, e.g., that you have never
met her husband or kids, that you saw this mail server accessed from
his IP, etc.

(Covering my ass note: I am not a lawyer, & I have not played one on tv.
No guarrantees are are provided with this advice, not even the expectation
that it may help. For qualified legal advice, contact an attorney with
experience in this area of the law.)

Q: You ask how to prevent a repeat of this security infringement.

A: Well, a good place to start would be to make her change the password,
wouldn't it? It's the weakest link in the entire setup. And since the
other folks in her life guessed her current password so easily, I'd
force her to change it to something that the usual tools like crack
determine is secure. Do some googling for other ideas.

As for technical solutions, unless her ex-husband is a computer security
guru, almost any UNIX-based system ought to work if you properly install
it,  configure it, & keep up with the necessary patches.

Q: ``I want to keep her as a friend."

A: Just as a gut reaction, wouldn't a friend believe you if you said you
didn't do it? And if keeping your existence a secret from the kids was
an order from a judge, wouldn't you expect that she'd make an effort at
keeping this email account a secret? (And if it's the only email account
she has, & needs it for work or keeping in touch with friends/family, why
didn't you create another account for this purpose?)

My point here is that something doesn't smell right. It could be this
woman doesn't want to work very hard at obeying the judge's orders
(which means that if you clean up this mess, she certain to create
another one for you to clean up), or there's more to this story than
you know or are telling us. A good hint which might be the case is
how secure of a password she's willing to accept: if she's wiling
to use a string with at least 8 characters, upper & lower case, &
special characters, then it's a good sign; if she only wants passwords
like "daisy" (it's her favorite flower), "joe" (her son's name),
or "mustang" (the car she owns), & won't even consider trivial
changes (e.g. to "daisY" or "da1sy" because she considers it "too
confusing"), it's a bad sign. But this part about the password should
be common sense to anyone who's a SysAdmin, & incurable lusers never
make good friends.

Geoff



From russj at dimstar.net  Sun Feb 27 13:32:34 2005
From: russj at dimstar.net (Russ Johnson)
Date: Sun, 27 Feb 2005 13:32:34 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Have to prove I got hacked...
In-Reply-To: <1109472204.422133cc79f54@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
References: <200502270137.j1R1bn7e008300@barrierb241.nike.com>
	<1109472204.422133cc79f54@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <42223C72.8070002@dimstar.net>

plug_0 at robinson-west.com wrote:

>The subject is what I'm suspecting, that I need to prove the ex
>came in and took email to both cover myself and help my friend.  
>I would appreciate some technical help to make my IMP system 
>safer.
>  
>
Most likely, a support list for that piece of software would be a good 
start. Others here on this list may be able to help, but most likely, 
the authors of that software have already documented setting up security.

Alternatively, I would check the logs for that software to find out 
where connections are coming from, and if the login was successful. This 
is NOT ironclad evidence that someone else was able to get in. It IS 
however, circumstantial that someone other than the owner was able to 
get in.

How they obtained necessary credentials is anyones guess. Again, logs 
may help you to show that someone else tried to get to the account.

All the other gobbledy-gook in your message has nothing to do with 
Linux, and should be taken elsewhere.

From ehem at m5p.com  Sun Feb 27 13:51:16 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Sun, 27 Feb 2005 13:51:16 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Graphics Programming with GTK+?
In-Reply-To: <20050227200012.B67B04231@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200502272151.j1RLpGkS019925@m5p.com>

>From: Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com>
>    Has anyone used gtk+ for graphics programming -- as distinct from a WIMP
> GUI?
> 
>    I want to build a GUI and X Window System capability onto a GIS
> application. The console UI for that app is 25-30 years out of date. My
> older book on developing linux applications with gtk+/gdk tells me that it
> does have functions to draw and manipulate (i.e., zoom, pan, query) vector
> and raster data on screen.
> 
>    If you have experience with this I'd appreciate your impressions of
> ease-of-use and suitability of the available functions (which, I imagine,
> are all in the gdk). This project has a second-tier priority so I'm not in a
> rush but I'd like to do some planning and learning in the interim.

Haven't done precisely what you're suggesting. I've talked directly to
Xlib for the rendering of this one program, since then I've pasted on a
front-end via GTK+v2. Took some doing, but the old direct Xlib interface
still works. Depending on precisely what you're doing, you might want to
use OpenGL functionality instead.

I like GTK+/GDK. They provide a very nice interface. If you need OpenGL's
functionality there are two libraries, GtkGLArea and GtkGLExt. Appears
the former is better known, while I suspect the latter is better
designed.

Elliott,

> functionality there are two libraries, GtkGLArea and GtkGLExt. Appears the
> former is better known, while I suspect the latter is better designed.

   There's Mesa as an equivalent to OpenGL for 3D and I've looked at LessTIF
for 2D work. Everything seems rather out of date, which really surprised me
when I went looking. I know that Qt has this capabilities but I'm much more
comfortable with C than with C++. In the Java world, I believe that Swing
has graphics support (but it did not look extensive at my quick glance at
the book), but SWT does not (at least, not according to my SWT Developer's
Handbook).

Rich

Michael,

Not recommended for normal production use but when one must...

  # ps -ef | grep pdfs | awk '{ print $2 }' | while read proc [enter]
  # do [enter]
   # kill -9 $proc [enter]
  # done


-Coop

From heinlein at madboa.com  Mon Feb 28 10:04:32 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Mon, 28 Feb 2005 10:04:32 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Kill
In-Reply-To: <20050228175354.GA20176@themontagnes.com>
References: <20050228175354.GA20176@themontagnes.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.62.0502281002410.919@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Mon, 28 Feb 2005, Michael Montagne wrote:

> So I made a neato cron job that ran every minute and now it has 
> locked up my server.  It calls gs to make pdfs.  I have MANY gs 
> processes running but I can't kill them.  I tried "killall gs" and 
> "kill-9 22884"  the machine is so slow, every step takes 5 minutes. 
> How can I stop these things.

First off, stop crond. That'll give you some breathing room. Then kill 
the errant gs processes. Then edit your crontab to remove the job or, 
perhaps, reduce its frequency so you can observe it more closely. Then 
restart crond.

--Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

Have you called 611 to find out if there are any updates for your phone?

updated to keep support.

Not trying to stop you from changing, but if you can avoid that 
"breaking the contract" part, that's money in your pocket.

> I've heard T-mobile is decent, as well as Nextel.

T-Mobile is lacking in coverage in Oregon. If you leave the metro area, 
you won't have service. I have friends in McMinnville that lose service 
in certain areas of that town because they don't have enough towers. 
She's been waiting for two years for them to add towers.

I know nothing about Nextel except they supply most of the construction 
industry because of their walkie talkie feature. (Be-Beep!)

I had AT&T up until just before the Cingular acquisition, loved the 
service, but the rest of the people I talk to have Verizon. So I 
switched, because of their "IN" calling. Kept my same phone number, and 
have pretty good service.

In-Reply-To: <20050228165246.7E0E34237@ulke.nakedape.cc>

> > front-end via GTK+v2. Took some doing, but the old direct Xlib interface

> 
> Elliott,
> 
>    I was trying to avoid very low level programming.

I figured, but I felt I should mention what I have done versus what I
merely have a very good feel for.

> > I like GTK+/GDK. They provide a very nice interface. If you need OpenGL's
> > functionality there are two libraries, GtkGLArea and GtkGLExt. Appears the
> > former is better known, while I suspect the latter is better designed.
> 
>    There's Mesa as an equivalent to OpenGL for 3D and I've looked at LessTIF
> for 2D work. Everything seems rather out of date, which really surprised me
> when I went looking. I know that Qt has this capabilities but I'm much more
> comfortable with C than with C++. In the Java world, I believe that Swing
> has graphics support (but it did not look extensive at my quick glance at
> the book), but SWT does not (at least, not according to my SWT Developer's
> Handbook).

GtkGLArea and GtkGLExt are binding libraries. They give you an interface
to the platform-specific setup needed for OpenGL. As such they give you
an interface that looks like GTK/GDK, rather than needing to directly
talk to Xlib. I'm still not certain you need to resort to OpenGL, just
that is possibility given your description.

Go back to the first two sentences of the original paragraph though, "I
like GTK+/GDK. They provide a very nice interface." I consider them to be
good, if you don't need the transformations or 3D of OpenGL they should
do very nicely by themselves.


--

From heinlein at madboa.com  Mon Feb 28 15:40:38 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Mon, 28 Feb 2005 15:40:38 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] loading lirc_gpio on boot
In-Reply-To: <200502282319.j1SNJs6J006673@barrierb241.nike.com>
References: <200502282319.j1SNJs6J006673@barrierb241.nike.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.62.0502281524240.919@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Mon, 28 Feb 2005, Anderson, Rob (Global Trade) wrote:

> Anyone? Please :)
>
>> I am able load the modules after the box is up by running "modprobe 
>> lirc_gpio" as root. I was under the impression that adding the 
>> above line to /etc/modprobe.conf was all that I needed to do in 
>> order to have this modules loaded at startup.

Linux distributions provide varying mechanisms for loading modules at 
boot time:

* Debian

   echo "lirc_gpio" >> /etc/modules

* Gentoo (modify target file to kernel-2.4 if appropriate)

   echo "lirc_gpio" >> /etc/modules.autoload.d/kernel-2.6

* Red Hat/Fedora

   echo "/sbin/modprobe lirc_gpio" >> /etc/rc.d/rc.local

* SuSE

   echo "/sbin/modprobe lirc_gpio" >> /etc/rc.d/boot.local

--Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

Is fixup-whitespace what you're looking for?

Try it (M-x fixup-whitespace<return>) to see if it does what you want.

I'm afraid that it doesn't come preset to a key combination, but it's 
pretty easy to define it as a key in your .emacs file.

One way would be:

(define-key global-map [some key here]      'fixup-whitespace)

Ali


PS:  Try 'C-h a whitespace' to see more possibilities fro dealing with
whitespace issues.

Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:

> On Mon, 28 Feb 2005, William A Morita wrote:
> 
> > If the cursor is over a blank or tab Alt-Space will reduce that space void
> > to a single space.  This may get you close to what you want.
> 
> Bill,
> 
>    Aha! That's exactly what I want to do: reduce a string of whitespace to a
> single space.
> 

To eliminate all space, use M-\

M-\ runs the command delete-horizontal-space
   which is an interactive compiled Lisp function in `simple'.
(delete-horizontal-space &optional BACKWARD-ONLY)

Delete all spaces and tabs around point.
If BACKWARD-ONLY is non-nil, only delete spaces before point.


galen

  I wouldn't recomend it.  Here are my measured latency stats for today:

Average RTT (for the day): 
--------------------------------------------------
Cur: 0.8607 seconds
Avg: 1.1571 seconds
Max: 8.2915 seconds

  GPRS also has a problem with slow startup after the remote gets

remote stays in the poll queue.  My RTT numbers are measured *after*
my monitor has sent a couple of pings to wake the network up.

From clydefrog at adnap.no-ip.com  Mon Feb 28 20:06:51 2005
From: clydefrog at adnap.no-ip.com (Evan Heidtmann)
Date: Mon, 28 Feb 2005 20:06:51 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Sorry -- php question
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502281618510.31125-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502281618510.31125-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
Message-ID: <1109650011.2555.17.camel@localhost.localdomain>

On Mon, 2005-02-28 at 18:53 -0800, Roderick A. Anderson wrote:
> index.php is simply doing a redirect to the developer(s) system but it 
> just shows up as text when I view the source.

What do you mean?

> Here is the content of their index.php with changes to to protect teh 
> guilty.
> 
> <?
> header("Location: http://inlt.example.com"); /* Redirect browser
>                                             to PHP web site */
> exit;                 /* Make sure that code below does
>                          not get executed when we redirect. */
> 
> ?>

This shouldn't be a php4 versus php5 issue; the code is pretty simple.
What's probably tripping you up is having a blank line or a space in
front of the opening <? tag. You might also try changing the opening tag
to <?php instead: you need short_open_tag set to "On" in php.ini for the
<? tag to work.

Evan



From bsr at spek.org  Mon Feb 28 20:07:57 2005
From: bsr at spek.org (Brent Rieck)
Date: Mon, 28 Feb 2005 20:07:57 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Sorry -- php question
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502281618510.31125-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0502281618510.31125-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
Message-ID: <4223EA9D.5010707@spek.org>

It looks like PHP might not be installed or is not configured quite 
right.  The header function is available in PHP4 and is being used 
correctly in your example.  Do other PHP things work on the server?

Assuming other PHP things work I'd check that "short_open_tag" directive 
is set to "on" in your php.ini or appropriate .htaccess file (or change 
the "<?" to "<?php" in your index.php file)

If no other PHP things work be sure lines approximating these are in 
your httpd configuration file(s) in the logical locations:
   LoadModule php4_module modules/libphp4.so
   AddModule mod_php4.c (not needed for apache 2)
   AddType application/x-httpd-php .php

--Brent

From kens at cad2cam.com  Mon Feb 28 20:16:39 2005
From: kens at cad2cam.com (Kenneth G. Stephens)
Date: Mon, 28 Feb 2005 20:16:39 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] loading lirc_gpio on boot
In-Reply-To: <Pine.OSX.4.62.0502281524240.919@arrowhead.galois.com>
References: <200502282319.j1SNJs6J006673@barrierb241.nike.com>
	<Pine.OSX.4.62.0502281524240.919@arrowhead.galois.com>
Message-ID: <1109650599.5818.14.camel@atlas.cadtocam.com>

On Mon, 2005-02-28 at 15:40 -0800, Paul Heinlein wrote:
> On Mon, 28 Feb 2005, Anderson, Rob (Global Trade) wrote:
> 
> > Anyone? Please :)
> >
> >> I am able load the modules after the box is up by running "modprobe 
> >> lirc_gpio" as root. I was under the impression that adding the 
> >> above line to /etc/modprobe.conf was all that I needed to do in 
> >> order to have this modules loaded at startup.
> 
> Linux distributions provide varying mechanisms for loading modules at 
> boot time:
> 
> * Debian
> 
>    echo "lirc_gpio" >> /etc/modules
> 
> * Gentoo (modify target file to kernel-2.4 if appropriate)
> 
>    echo "lirc_gpio" >> /etc/modules.autoload.d/kernel-2.6
> 
> * Red Hat/Fedora
> 
>    echo "/sbin/modprobe lirc_gpio" >> /etc/rc.d/rc.local
> 
> * SuSE
> 
>    echo "/sbin/modprobe lirc_gpio" >> /etc/rc.d/boot.local
> 
> --Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

You may also want to run as root depmod -a to recreate the
dependencies. 
-- 
Ken Stephens
CAD 2 CAM

Maodhog <techmage at aracnet.com> wrote:

> 
> I took all the routers and cables over to a friend at PCC and had the
> cis lab test out everything. Verdict: everything worked as per cisco
> standard.
> 
> was told to check serial port.
> 
> Now I know it was working, but just to be sure I swapped out the
> connector that runs from the Motherboard to external on the case.
> 

Just in case you didn't know, there are two wiring standards for the
motherboard serial cable.  They are sometimes referred to as the
ASUS/Everest wiring and the DTK/Intel wiring.  Obviously it's important
to use the one that matches the motherboard wiring.

Of course, yours could just be broken.

galen

On Mon, 2005-02-28 at 12:09 -0800, Brent Jones wrote:
> Off-topic, but I'm fed up with my current provider (ATT/Cingular)

So were we.  We're now using Nextel...

> And I figured some people on PLUG are pretty mobile, and would have some 
> other recomendations on cellphone providers.
> For the last two months or so, I've been getting tons of dropped calls, 
> when I have perfectly good reception. Infuriating.

Yup.  Sounds like exactly what I saw.

> And starting this weekend, people are getting "number disconnected", or 
> straight to my voice mail, without my phone even ringing.

Don't you just love that?  Try coming down to St. Paul some time.
Crappiest signal anywhere... the phone beeps instead of dialing half the
time.  Call up AT&T and ask them about it.  They'll tell you you should
have a full signal because there are towers "all around you" ... uh-huh.

> So, its come to the point where I break my contract, and find a new 
> provider.

It's $175 to break the contract.  You may be able to drop your plan down
to next-to-nothing and avoid the contract break (but be unable to keep
your phone number).

> I've heard T-mobile is decent, as well as Nextel.
> But I was wondering what PLUGgers have experience with.

I'm using Nextel now... most of my family does, many friends do.  The
"DirectConnect" thing is pretty cool.  Where the signal is marginal, the
quality is awesome.

However, their coverage map isn't the best in the world.  The maps on
their websites are accurate.  I carry my old AT&T phone with me when I
travel in case I do need to make a 911 call in a non-Nextel area.

I've had good luck with them so far, though.  When traveling in Southern
California and Georgia during the last few months I didn't run in to any
dead zones except inside an old hotel.

Essentially, if you're fine with the coverage maps and the higher price,
Nextel is a good company to get cell phone service from.  They *do*
nickel and dime you a bit... so except your bill to be a little bit
higher than the rep may imply to you.
